- *See: [`Renderer.h`](Renderer.h), [`GUIManager.h`](GUIManager.h), [`GUIManager.cpp`](GUIManager.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderer.h`](OpenGLRenderer.h), [`OpenGLRenderer.cpp`](OpenGLRenderer.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`DX11Renderer.h`](DX11Renderer.h), [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.h`](VULKAN_Renderer.h), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp), [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp), [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp)*

- **Fix — Quit-to-Desktop button: music continues and window hangs on DX12** (`GUIWindows.cpp`):
  The `FadeOutThenCallback` lambda (fires from render thread) was missing `StopMusicPlayback()` and called `PostMessage(WM_CLOSE)` while the render thread was still mid-frame. Fixed: added `extern void StopMusicPlayback()` + call it first; replaced the direct `PostMessage` with a detached `std::thread` that sleeps 100 ms (≥ 6 frames at 60fps) to let the render thread safely finish before posting `WM_CLOSE` to the main thread.
- *See: [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 starfield visually slower than DX11** (`DX12FXManager.cpp`):
  Star velocity initialised to `[20, 60]` units/second — identical to DX11 in source, but DX11's static `lastTweenTime` accumulated a growing delta that effectively accelerated stars. DX12's correctly-clamped 60fps delta of 0.016s produced noticeably slower apparent motion. Tripled spawn and respawn speed to `[60, 180]` units/second for visual parity with DX11.
- *See: [`DX12FXManager.cpp`](DX12FXManager.cpp)*

- **Feature — GPU capability detection in DX11, Vulkan and OpenGL renderers** (`DX11Renderer.h/.cpp`, `VULKAN_Renderer.h/.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderer.h/.cpp`):
  Mirrors the DX12 capability detection added earlier. Each renderer adds `m_dedicatedVRAMMB`, `m_sharedSystemMemMB`, `m_isUMA`, `m_isLowEndGPU`. DX11 queries `DXGI_ADAPTER_DESC` via `IDXGIDevice::GetAdapter`. Vulkan queries `VkPhysicalDeviceMemoryProperties` heap sizes and `deviceType` for UMA detection. OpenGL adds `dxgi.lib` + `<dxgi.h>` (Windows guard) and enumerates the default DXGI adapter for VRAM; GPU name from `glGetString(GL_RENDERER/GL_VENDOR)`.
- *See: [`DX11Renderer.h`](DX11Renderer.h), [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.h`](VULKAN_Renderer.h), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderer.h`](OpenGLRenderer.h), [`OpenGLRenderer.cpp`](OpenGLRenderer.cpp)*

- **Feature — Buffering config option + Triple Buffering UI toggle + per-tab scrollbars** (`Configuration.h`, `Configuration.cpp`, `GUIConfigWindow.cpp`, `DX11Renderer.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.h`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`, `VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`):
  Added `int buffering = 1` (1=triple, 0=double) to `MyConfig`. The field is persisted to `GameConfig.cfg` via `loadConfig`/`saveConfig` and included in the FNV-1a checksum so tampering is detected. Under the **Video** tab a new **Triple Buffering** toggle slider (id `t2_tripbuf`) sets `buffering` and marks `needsVideoRestart`; the toggle initialises from the current config value. All renderers now read the setting at swap-chain creation time: DX11 sets `swapDesc.BufferCount` to 3 or 2; DX12 introduces a new private member `m_effectiveFrameCount` (3 or 2) that replaces the compile-time `FrameCount = 3` constant in `CreateSwapChain`, `CreateRenderTargetViews`, `CreateD2DRenderTargets`, and `Resize`'s `ResizeBuffers`/RTV-recreation loops (cleanup and max-allocation loops keep `FrameCount` so nothing is leaked); Vulkan sets `ci.minImageCount` from `minImageCount + 1` (triple) or `minImageCount` (double), clamped to `maxImageCount`. The Video tab now has 12 rows, which exceeds the 370 px visible height by 14 px. Added a 12-pixel-wide vertical scrollbar to every tab's content area: scroll state (`tabScrollY[5]`) is a `shared_ptr<std::array<float,5>>`; `setTabScroll(delta)` shifts the Y positions of visible tab controls and clamps to `[0, contentH − 370]`; `doSwitchTab` un-scrolls the outgoing tab before switching; the scrollbar thumb is drawn via `onCustomRender`; mouse-wheel is routed via `onMouseWheel` (18 px/notch); clicking the track jumps to the proportional position via `onCustomMouseInput`. All horizontal sliders are narrowed by `CFG_SCROLL_W + 4 = 16 px` and the info-row value label uses the same budget so no control overlaps the scrollbar track.
- *See: [`Configuration.h`](Configuration.h), [`Configuration.cpp`](Configuration.cpp), [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp), [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — OpenGL Release build LNK4098: LIBCMT conflicts with MSVCRT** (`CMakeLists.txt`, `build/OpenGL/Release/CrossPlatformGameEngine.vcxproj`):
  `glew32s.lib` was compiled `/MT` and pulls `LIBCMT.lib` as a default lib. The project's Release config uses `/MD` (`MultiThreadedDLL` → `MSVCRT.lib`). Having both causes `LNK4098: defaultlib 'LIBCMT' conflicts`. Debug was already protected by `/NODEFAULTLIB:LIBCMT`. Fixed by adding the same flag to the CMake Release generator expression and patching `IgnoreSpecificDefaultLibraries` directly in the already-generated vcxproj Release `Link` block.
- *See: [`CMakeLists.txt`](CMakeLists.txt), [`build/OpenGL/Release/CrossPlatformGameEngine.vcxproj`](build/OpenGL/Release/CrossPlatformGameEngine.vcxproj)*

- **Feature — DX12 low-end GPU support: feature level cascade + capability detection** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.h`):
  `CreateDevice()` and `SelectBestAdapter()` hard-coded `D3D_FEATURE_LEVEL_12_0` as the minimum for `D3D12CreateDevice`, silently rejecting GPUs that support DX12 only at FL 11.1 (many Intel HD/Iris, older AMD APUs). Changed minimum to `D3D_FEATURE_LEVEL_11_0` in both locations — the device is still created at the adapter's maximum supported level, so no functionality is lost on capable hardware. After device creation, added a GPU capability query block that populates six new private members: `m_dedicatedVRAMMB`, `m_sharedSystemMemMB` (VRAM in MB from `DXGI_ADAPTER_DESC3`); `m_isUMA` (`D3D12_FEATURE_DATA_ARCHITECTURE.UMA`); `m_isLowEndGPU` (true when VRAM < 2 GB or UMA); `m_maxFeatureLevel` (`D3D12_FEATURE_DATA_FEATURE_LEVELS`); `m_resourceBindingTier` (`D3D12_FEATURE_DATA_D3D12_OPTIONS.ResourceBindingTier`). All six are logged at startup and available for future runtime quality-scaling decisions.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h)*

- **Fix — DX12 pipeline 6fps: per-frame COM resource creation through 11on12 layer** (`DX12Renderer.h`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`, `DX12RenderFrame.cpp`):
  Every call to `DrawMyText`, `DrawMyTextStyled`, `DrawMyTextWithFont`, `DrawMyTextCentered`, and `DrawRectangle` created a new `IDWriteTextFormat` and `ID2D1SolidColorBrush`. Through the 11on12 compatibility layer each creation carries significant synchronisation overhead; with 10+ creates per frame at 60 Hz the accumulated cost dropped throughput to ~6fps. Added two per-renderer caches: `m_generalBrush` (`ID2D1SolidColorBrush`) is created once and reused via `SetColor()` on every text/rect call; `m_textFormatCache` (`unordered_map<wstring, IDWriteTextFormat*>`) caches by (fontName|fontSize|weight|style) key. Private helpers `GetOrCreateTextFormat()` and `SetGeneralBrushColor()` encapsulate the lookup/creation logic. The renderer-info overlay in `DX12RenderFrame.cpp` was also updated to use the cached format. Both caches are released in `Cleanup()` before the 11on12 device is torn down.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11 heap corruption: `AddEffect` unprotected `push_back` during render iteration** (`DX_FXManager.h`, `DX_FXManager.cpp`):
  The DX11 `FXManager::AddEffect()` called `effects.push_back()` without checking `bIsRendering`, the same guard present in the DX12 path. If the loader thread (breadcrumb: `LoaderTaskThread` + `RenderFrame` both active) called `AddEffect` while the render thread was iterating `effects` inside `Render()`, a vector reallocation occurred mid-iteration. The reallocation moved `FXItem` objects to new storage and called `~FXItem()` on the old elements; `TextFadeData::~TextFadeData` tried to free a `wstring` whose heap block had already been corrupted by the concurrent write, producing the `_CrtIsValidHeapPointer(block)` assertion at `debug_heap.cpp:904`. Fixed by adding `std::vector<FXItem> m_pendingEffects` to `DX_FXManager.h` and mirroring the DX12 deferred-push pattern: `AddEffect` uses the `bIsRendering` guard + `m_effectsMutex` to defer into `m_pendingEffects`; `Render()` flushes the pending list to `effects` after `RemoveCompletedEffects()` — identical to the DX12FXManager approach.
- *See: [`DX_FXManager.h`](DX_FXManager.h), [`DX_FXManager.cpp`](DX_FXManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — MoviePlayer `CreateVideoTexture` missing return value for Vulkan/OpenGL pipelines** (`MoviePlayer.cpp`):
  `CreateVideoTexture` had `#if __USE_DIRECTX_12__ ... #elif __USE_DIRECTX_11__ ... #endif` with no `#else` branch. For Vulkan and OpenGL (neither define active) the function body was empty, causing `error C4716: must return a value`. Added `#else return true;` — Vulkan/OpenGL use the CPU-buffer path (`UpdateVideoTextureCPU`) and require no GPU texture object from this function.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 pipeline sustained 6fps: D2D double-flush, redundant locks, double buffering** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.h`):
  Three changes combined: (1) Two-pass D2D design (separate BeginDraw/EndDraw for background and overlay) merged into a single BeginDraw/EndDraw — each `EndDraw` flushed D2D batches to the 11on12 device, doubling translation overhead per frame. (2) `ThreadLockHelper d2dClearLock` around `ClearRenderTargetView`/`ClearDepthStencilView` (D3D12 command-list ops, no D2D relevance) and `ThreadLockHelper d2dRenderLock` (render thread is sole D2D user) were both removed. (3) `FrameCount` raised from 2 to 3 — double buffering caused `Present(1,0)` to block waiting for the previous buffer; the third buffer allows the CPU to pipeline one frame ahead without stalling. `BeginDraw` was also moved inside the shutdown guard to prevent a BeginDraw without EndDraw during graceful exit.
- *See: [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h)*

- **Fix — DX12 GameMenu position formula used magic number 300** (`GUIManager.h`, `GUIWindows.cpp`, `GUIManager.cpp`):
  Added `GAMEMENU_WINDOW_WIDTH = 300` constant to `GUIManager.h`; replaced all three hardcoded `300` occurrences with the constant so the formula is explicitly `iOrigWidth - GAMEMENU_WINDOW_WIDTH`.
- *See: [`GUIManager.h`](GUIManager.h), [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp), [`GUIManager.cpp`](GUIManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 Configuration window 20px too tall** (`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`):
  Added `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)` guard: config window height is 460px on DX12, 480px on all other pipelines.
- *See: [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 startup error: `GetContainingOutput` fails when window not yet on a display** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  `SetFullScreen()` and `SetFullExclusive()` hard-failed on `GetContainingOutput` failure. At startup (displayMode=2) the swap chain may not yet be associated with an output. Both functions now downgrade to WARNING and fall back to the adapter's first output via `IDXGIDevice::GetAdapter` → `IDXGIAdapter::EnumOutputs(0)`.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 intro movie plays twice** (`main.cpp`):
  The `FadeOutThenCallback` lambda called `OpenMovieAndPlay()` but left `scene.bSceneSwitching = true`, causing the main loop's `bSceneSwitching && !IsFadeActive()` check to call `SwitchToMovieIntro()` → `OpenMovieAndPlay()` a second time. Added `scene.bSceneSwitching = false` inside the callback.
- *See: [`main.cpp`](main.cpp)*

- **Feature — Renderer init log now shows renderer type** (`RendererFactory.cpp`):
  `CreateRendererInstance()` logged a generic "Renderer instance created" message. Replaced with `#if`-chained: `"DirectX 12 renderer instance successfully initialised."`, `"DirectX 11 …"`, `"Vulkan …"`, `"OpenGL …"`.
- *See: [`RendererFactory.cpp`](RendererFactory.cpp)*

- **Feature — Auto-correct config rendererType to match compiled pipeline before renderer creation** (`main.cpp`):
  If the saved config `rendererType` doesn't match the compiled pipeline (e.g. config was last written by a DX11 build but the DX12 binary is now running), the mismatch was silently ignored — any subsystem that read `rendererType` at startup would see the wrong value. Added a validation block in `WinMain` immediately before `CreateRendererInstance()`: `compiledRendererType` is resolved from the active `#if __USE_DIRECTX_11__ / _12__ / __USE_OPENGL__ / __USE_VULKAN__` define, per-platform values applied (Windows: 0=DX11, 1=DX12, 2=OGL, 3=VK; Linux/Android: 0=OGL, 1=VK; iOS/macOS: 0). If the value differs from `config.myConfig.rendererType`, the config is overridden and `config.saveConfig()` is called before the renderer is instantiated. A WARNING-level log entry records the mismatch and the corrected value.
- *See: [`main.cpp`](main.cpp)*

- **Fix — LOG_ERROR now terminates the application** (`Debug.cpp`):
  `LOG_CRITICAL` and `LOG_TERMINATION` already called `PostQuitMessage(EXIT_FAILURE)`. `LOG_ERROR` did not — after a RenderFrame exception the render thread logged the error and returned, leaving the app running with no rendering. Extended the `PostQuitMessage` guard to include `LOG_ERROR` so any error-level log triggers a clean main-loop exit.
- *See: [`Debug.cpp`](Debug.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan game-menu buttons not bold** (`GUIWindows.cpp`):
  All six game-menu buttons now have `bold = true` under `#if defined(__USE_OPENGL__) || defined(__USE_VULKAN__)`, matching the existing OpenGL-only bold that was already in place.
- *See: [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan config window: no clipping and text not rendering** (`VULKAN_Renderer.h`, `VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`, `GUIConfigWindow.cpp`):
  `VulkanRenderer` had no `PushClipRect`/`PopClipRect` implementations — tab-content controls bled outside the bevel. Added D2D `PushAxisAlignedClip`/`PopAxisAlignedClip` implementation (same as DX11). Config window bottom-button bold extended to `|| defined(__USE_VULKAN__)`.
- *See: [`VULKAN_Renderer.h`](VULKAN_Renderer.h), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp), [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp)*

- **Feature — Config window: custom 3D drawn titlebar with circular close button** (`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`, `Renderer.h`, all renderer implementations):
  Replaced the `IMG_TITLEBAR1` texture titlebar with a renderer-drawn 3D-style bar: dark navy base, 2 px blue highlight edge at top, 1 px shadow at bottom, title text centred. A crimson circular close button is drawn at `(WX + WW − 15, titlebar centre Y)` radius 8.5 px with outer dark ring and `×` glyph. Clicking the circle cancels (reverts config) and closes the window. ESC key (via `KBHandlersCode.cpp`) also fires the Close-button handler for revert + close. Added `DrawCircle(center, radius, color, filled)` to `Renderer.h` and all four pipelines: DX11/DX12/Vulkan use D2D `FillEllipse`/`DrawEllipse`; OpenGL uses horizontal scanline rectangles.
- *See: [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp), [`KBHandlersCode.cpp`](KBHandlersCode.cpp), [`Renderer.h`](Renderer.h), [`DX11Renderer.h`](DX11Renderer.h), [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.h`](VULKAN_Renderer.h), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderer.h`](OpenGLRenderer.h), [`OpenGLRenderer.cpp`](OpenGLRenderer.cpp)*

  `SCROLL_H = CONT_H − 8.0f` → `CONT_H − 11.0f` (−3 px per spec).

- **Fix — DX12 app hangs on exit: `WaitForGPUToFinish` uses 5-second fence timeout during shutdown** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  `WaitForGPUToFinish()` (called from `Cleanup()`) waited up to 5 seconds unconditionally. Changed to mirror `WaitForPreviousFrame`: use 500 ms when `bIsShuttingDown` is true, 5000 ms otherwise. Prevents a 5-second hang at the end of every exit sequence.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan cascading crash: validation-layer errors mapped to LOG_ERROR triggering PostQuitMessage** (`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`):
  The Vulkan debug-utils messenger callback (line ~475) mapped `VK_DEBUG_UTILS_MESSAGE_SEVERITY_ERROR` → `LOG_ERROR`. Now that `LOG_ERROR` calls `PostQuitMessage`, a `vkDestroySampler` validation warning during normal scene cleanup was triggering a shutdown mid-frame, cascading into NULL-image pipeline barriers, thread-pool crashes, and access violations in `LoadTexture`. Fixed by mapping validation-layer messages to `LOG_WARNING` / `LOG_DEBUG` (diagnostic only, not fatal).
- *See: [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan `vkDestroySampler` validation error during scene cleanup** (`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`):
  `DestroyVulkanTexture` destroyed samplers, image views, images, and memory without waiting for GPU work referencing those resources to complete. Added `vkDeviceWaitIdle(m_device)` at the start of `DestroyVulkanTexture` so all queued commands drain before any resource is freed.
- *See: [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan NULL-image pipeline barrier in `UploadOverlayToVulkan`** (`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`):
  Added explicit `m_overlayTexture.image != VK_NULL_HANDLE` guard before the `vkCmdPipelineBarrier` call so a partially-initialised overlay texture cannot produce a validation error.
- *See: [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — Config window circular close button not responding to clicks; saves instead of reverting** (`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`):
  The previous implementation relied on `onCustomMouseInput` with captured-at-creation-time coordinates, which (a) could mismatch after window drag and (b) was never firing reliably. Replaced with a transparent `Button` control ("btn_circleclose") at the circle location — `MoveWindow` keeps it in sync after dragging. `onMouseBtnDown` saves the config (`config.saveConfig()`) then closes, with an `std::atomic<bool>` guard against double-fire. `onCustomRender` now reads all positions live from `weakWin->position` so the circle, title text, and scrollbar all stay correct after dragging.
- *See: [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp)*

#### June 06, 2026

- **Fix — DX12 ScreenRecorder captures no video (blank recording)** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`):
  `DX12RenderFrame.cpp` contained the blinking REC indicator (`IsRecording()` check) but never called `screenRecorder.CaptureFrame()`. All other pipelines (DX11 in `DXRenderFrame.cpp`, Vulkan in `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`, OpenGL in `OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`) call `CaptureFrame` before their respective `Present` call; the DX12 equivalent was simply omitted. Added the call immediately before `PresentFrame()`, after `ReleaseWrappedResources()` + `Flush()` have transitioned the back buffer to `D3D12_RESOURCE_STATE_PRESENT` — the exact state `CaptureFrame` expects before issuing its PRESENT→COPY_SOURCE→PRESENT barrier pair.
- *See: [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11 `CreateVideoTexture` fails with E_INVALIDARG (0x80070057): SRV created from staging texture** (`MoviePlayer.cpp`):
  `CreateVideoTexture` (DX11 path) created `m_videoTexture` as `D3D11_USAGE_STAGING` with `BindFlags = 0`, then immediately called `CreateShaderResourceView` on it. D3D11 staging textures have no bind flags and cannot be bound to the pipeline; `CreateShaderResourceView` returned `E_INVALIDARG`, causing `OpenMovie` to abort with "Failed to create video texture". Fix: after the staging texture is successfully created, a second DEFAULT texture (`m_videoRenderTexture`) is created with `D3D11_BIND_SHADER_RESOURCE`; the SRV is built from that texture. The existing `CopyResource(m_videoRenderTexture, m_videoTexture)` call in `UpdateVideoTexture` then copies each decoded frame from the CPU-writable staging texture into the shader-visible DEFAULT texture on every rendered frame.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 pipeline hangs on shutdown (process survives after window closes)** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`, `ScreenRecorder.cpp`):
  `DX12Renderer::Cleanup()` never set `threadManager.threadVars.bIsShuttingDown = true`, unlike DX11 which sets it as its very first action. Consequences: (1) `WaitForGPUToFinish()` and `WaitForPreviousFrame()` used the 5000ms fence timeout instead of the 500ms shutdown timeout; (2) the render thread loop's `!bIsShuttingDown.load()` exit condition never fired, leaving the render thread alive after `TerminateThread` returned. Fix mirrors the DX11 pattern: `bIsShuttingDown.store(true)` is now the first action after the `bHasCleanedUp` guard, `StopThread` is called before each `TerminateThread`, and the erroneous internal `threadManager.Cleanup()` call (which main.cpp already issues) is removed. Also fixed: `ScreenRecorder.cpp`'s DX11 `CaptureFrame` overload was being compiled in DX12 builds (which also define `__USE_DIRECTX_11__` for 11on12), referencing `m_stagingTexture` which is excluded from DX12 builds by the `#elif` header guard. Added `&& !defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)` to the `CaptureFrame` DX11 body guard.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`ScreenRecorder.cpp`](ScreenRecorder.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 ScreenRecorder `CaptureFrame` typo: `m_d3dDevice` → `m_d3d12Device`** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`):
  The `CaptureFrame` call added for Bug 2 used `m_d3dDevice` (DX11 naming) instead of the correct DX12 member `m_d3d12Device`, causing a C2065 compile error. Corrected to `m_d3d12Device`. Build now produces `DX12CPGE.exe` cleanly.
- *See: [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 ScreenRecorder captures blank video (format mismatch + no channel swap)** (`ScreenRecorder.cpp`):
  The DX12 `CaptureFrame` hardcoded `DXGI_FORMAT_B8G8R8A8_UNORM` in the `CopyTextureRegion` placed footprint, but the DX12 swap chain uses `DXGI_FORMAT_R8G8B8A8_UNORM`. D3D12 requires the footprint format to exactly match the source texture format; the mismatch caused the copy command list to enter an error state and `Close()` to fail, so `WriteVideoFrame` was never called and the video stream had zero frames. Fix: footprint format changed to `bbDesc.Format` (the actual back-buffer format). Additionally, the DX12 back buffer is RGBA byte order while the MF ARGB32 encoder input expects BGRA; added an in-place R↔B channel swap (`(v & 0xFF00FF00) | (R<<16) | (B>>16)`) over every pixel before passing the mapped data to `WriteVideoFrame`.
- *See: [`ScreenRecorder.cpp`](ScreenRecorder.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 process hangs after window closes (post-cleanup null dereference in `SetWindowedScreen`)** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  `main.cpp` calls `renderer->SetWindowedScreen()` on line 1682 immediately after `renderer->Cleanup()` on line 1680. After `Cleanup()`, `m_commandQueue`, `m_fence`, and `m_swapChain` are all null (ComPtr reset). `SetWindowedScreen()` called `WaitForGPUToFinish()` which dereferenced the null `m_commandQueue`, putting the process into an unrecoverable state that prevents clean exit. Two guards added: `if (bHasCleanedUp) return false;` at the top of `SetWindowedScreen()`, and `if (!m_commandQueue || !m_fence || !m_fenceEvent) return;` at the top of `WaitForGPUToFinish()`. The first guard short-circuits the entire call; the second is a defence-in-depth safety net for any other callers.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **New Feature — Ground-up FBX 7.x importer (`FBXImport.h`, `FBXImport.cpp`)**:
  Implemented a complete FBX file importer with no Autodesk SDK dependency. The importer handles both binary FBX 7.4/7.5 (Blender, Maya, 3ds Max exports) and ASCII FBX. Supports all nine required data types: (1) vertices and polygon triangulation with fan tessellation; (2) UV maps with FBX V-flip correction; (3) animation system — AnimationStack/Layer/CurveNode/Curve pipeline with X/Y/Z curve sampling, quaternion conversion from FBX Euler degrees, and conversion to `GLTFAnimation` format for the existing `GLTFAnimator`; (4) materials — Lambert, Phong, and PBR-like with diffuse/normal/specular/roughness/metallic/AO/emissive texture resolution; (5) lights — Point, Directional, Spot, Area with intensity, range, cone angles, shadow flags; (6) cameras — FOV, near/far planes, aspect ratio; (7) parent/child hierarchy via FBX `Connections OO` resolution; (8) tangents — extracted from `LayerElementTangent` or computed via Lengyel's method when absent; (9) shadow data — `CastShadow`/`ReceiveShadow` from `Properties70`. Compressed binary arrays use the Windows Compression API (`Cabinet.lib` MSZIP+COMPRESS_RAW) to decompress zlib DEFLATE payloads without external dependencies. Coordinate system is auto-detected from `GlobalSettings UpAxis` (Y-up or Z-up) and converted to the engine's left-handed Y-up world space.
- *See: [`FBXImport.h`](FBXImport.h), [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **New Feature — `SceneManager::ParseFBXScene()` and `ParseSceneAutoDetect()`** (`SceneManager.h`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  Added `ParseFBXScene()` to `SceneManager` which loads an FBX file via `FBXImporter`, registers lights in `lightsManager`, applies the first camera to the renderer, instantiates all mesh nodes into `scene_models[]` with correct parent/child slots, sets up GPU buffers via `SetupModelForRendering()`, and writes cache entries back to `models[]` for scene-revisit fast-path reuse. Added `ParseSceneAutoDetect()` which inspects the file extension (`.glb`, `.gltf`, `.fbx`) or binary magic bytes to automatically dispatch to `ParseGLBScene`, `ParseGLTFScene`, or `ParseFBXScene` with no caller changes required.
- *See: [`SceneManager.h`](SceneManager.h), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

#### June 07, 2026

- **Enhancement — ExceptionHandler extended to catch DEBUG alerts, CRT assert/error reports, invalid parameters, pure virtual calls, `std::terminate`, and `std::bad_alloc`** (`ExceptionHandler.h`, `ExceptionHandler.cpp`):
  The handler previously caught only SEH exceptions (Windows) and POSIX signals (Unix). Six additional trap points added — all Windows/CRT-specific ones wrapped in `#if defined(_WIN32) || defined(_WIN64)` guards; the C++ runtime ones are cross-platform:
  - **`_CrtSetReportHook2` (debug builds only)** — intercepts every `_ASSERT`, `_ASSERTE`, `_RPT*`, and internal CRT diagnostic before the CRT dialog fires. Logs type (`CRT Warning / CRT Error / CRT Assert`) and the full message; for errors and asserts also captures a stack trace and writes the call-stack log file.
  - **`_set_invalid_parameter_handler`** — catches CRT functions receiving illegal arguments (e.g. `printf(NULL)`, `vsnprintf` with zero buffer). Logs expression, function, file, and line; captures stack trace; generates a crash dump if enabled.
  - **`_set_purecall_handler`** — catches pure-virtual-function calls on incompletely constructed/destructed objects. Logs, captures stack, dumps.
  - **`signal(SIGABRT, ...)` + `_set_abort_behavior`** — intercepts `abort()`, failed CRT assertions in release, and any `raise(SIGABRT)`. The default CRT abort dialog is suppressed (`_WRITE_ABORT_MSG | _CALL_REPORTFAULT` cleared) so the handler is the sole responder; restored in `Cleanup()`.
  - **`std::set_terminate`** — catches unhandled C++ exceptions that reach `terminate()`. Uses `std::current_exception()` + re-throw to identify the exception type and message before dumping and chaining to the previous handler.
  - **`std::set_new_handler`** — catches `operator new` allocation failures. Logs the OOM condition, captures stack, then restores the previous handler and re-throws `std::bad_alloc` so callers receive the standard error.
  Constructor initialises all new members to safe sentinel values; `Cleanup()` restores every previous handler and reverses `_set_abort_behavior`. `GetExceptionDescription` extended with `STATUS_STACK_BUFFER_OVERRUN` (0xC0000409 — `/GS` cookie check), `STATUS_INVALID_CRUNTIME_PARAMETER` (0xC0000417), `STATUS_FATAL_APP_EXIT` (0x40000015), the MSVC C++ SEH code (0xE06D7363), and three debug exception codes (`DBG_CONTROL_C`, `DBG_PRINTEXCEPTION_C`, `DBG_RIPEXCEPTION`).
- *See: [`ExceptionHandler.h`](ExceptionHandler.h), [`ExceptionHandler.cpp`](ExceptionHandler.cpp)*

- **Feature — DX12 Models, Lighting, Materials and Textures** (`DX12Models.cpp`, `Models.h`, `DX12Renderer.h`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  The DX12 `RenderDX12()` draw path previously bound only the per-model camera/world constant buffer (b0) and rendered geometry with null texture descriptors. Lighting (b1), materials (b4), debug mode (b2), and actual texture SRVs were entirely absent, leaving models as flat white/unlit geometry.
  **Constant buffers (b1/b4/b2):** Three native DX12 upload-heap constant buffers (persistently mapped, 256-byte aligned) are now created in `SetupModelForRendering()` for the per-model light buffer (b1, min 1728 bytes to match shader contract), PBR material buffer (b4, 112 bytes), and pixel-shader debug buffer (b2, 16 bytes). `RenderDX12()` populates and binds all three every frame via `SetGraphicsRootConstantBufferView`, exactly mirroring the DX11 11on12-path `Render()` logic.
  **Textures (t0-t5):** `SetupModelForRendering()` allocates 6 consecutive SRV descriptor slots in the renderer's CBV/SRV/UAV heap (under `globalMutex`), storing the GPU handle in `ModelInfo::d3d12TextureGPUHandle`. On the **first render frame** for each model, `RegisterDX12Textures()` is called from `RenderDX12()` (render thread, command list open). It uses `ID3D11On12Device2::UnwrapUnderlyingResource` to obtain the native `ID3D12Resource` from each of the model's DX11-on-12 SRVs (diffuse/normal/metallic/roughness/AO/environment), creates typed SRV descriptors from the actual resource format, and records `COMMON → PIXEL_SHADER_RESOURCE` barriers on the open command list so the GPU transitions each texture before the draw call reads it. Slots with no source SRV (optional PBR maps) receive null descriptors. All subsequent frames bind the pre-built descriptor table handle directly.
  **Heap size:** The CBV/SRV/UAV descriptor heap was `MAX_TEXTURE_BUFFERS_3D + 10 = 12` slots — far too small for per-model SRVs. Increased to `DX12_MODEL_TEXTURE_HEAP_BASE + DX12_MODEL_TEXTURE_HEAP_CAPACITY = 12300` slots (null block + scene textures + 2048 models × 6 SRVs). `currentOffset` is initialised to `DX12_MODEL_TEXTURE_HEAP_BASE` after the null SRVs are written so allocations start at the correct position.
- *See: [`DX12Models.cpp`](DX12Models.cpp), [`Models.h`](Models.h), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 crash: access violation in `RegisterDX12Textures` inside d3d11.dll** (`DX12Models.cpp`, `Models.h`):
  The original `RegisterDX12Textures` called `ID3D11On12Device2::UnwrapUnderlyingResource` from the render thread while a DX12 command list was open. Internally `UnwrapUnderlyingResource` triggers `ID3D11DeviceContext::Flush()`, which flushes pending D2D commands and corrupts D3D11 state mid-frame, causing an access violation inside `d3d11.dll`. Root cause traced from the runtime stack: `Model::RegisterDX12Textures` → `Model::RenderDX12` → `DX12Renderer::RenderGamePlay` → `DX12Renderer::RenderFrame`.
  **Fix:** Eliminated all `UnwrapUnderlyingResource` / D3D11 calls from the render path entirely. Instead, raw RGBA pixel data is now cached in the `Texture` struct during load (`m_dx12PixelCache`, `m_dx12Width`, `m_dx12Height` — DX12-guarded members added to `Models.h`). A new `UploadDX12TextureToGPU` helper (loader thread, never render thread) creates a DEFAULT-heap `Texture2D` in `COPY_DEST` state, uploads pixels via an UPLOAD-heap buffer and `CopyTextureRegion`, then issues a `COPY_DEST → PIXEL_SHADER_RESOURCE` barrier and waits on a local per-call fence before returning. `SetupModelForRendering` calls this helper for each texture slot and frees the pixel cache immediately after upload. `RegisterDX12Textures` is now a pure CPU SRV-descriptor write with no barriers or D3D11 calls — resources are already in `PIXEL_SHADER_RESOURCE` state when the render thread first sees them. Shared texture pointers (metallic == roughness combined map) are detected by `shared_ptr` comparison to avoid redundant uploads.
- *See: [`DX12Models.cpp`](DX12Models.cpp), [`Models.h`](Models.h)*

- **Fix — DX12 Configuration window height increased by 10** (`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`):
  The DX12 `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)` branch window height was 456px; raised to 466px to match content.
- *See: [`GUIConfigWindow.cpp`](GUIConfigWindow.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11 GameMenu button text not vertically centred** (`DX11Renderer.cpp`):
  `DrawMyTextCentered` was passing the full button rect to `DrawText` and relying on `DWRITE_PARAGRAPH_ALIGNMENT_CENTER` for vertical centering. This is unreliable on `ID2D1RenderTarget` (DXGI surface) at non-96-DPI system scales — text remained top-aligned in practice. Fix: create an `IDWriteTextLayout` with a large unconstrained bounds, call `GetMetrics()` to obtain the actual rendered text width and height, then manually compute `centredX = position.x + controlWidth*0.5 - metrics.width*0.5` and `centredY = position.y + controlHeight*0.5 - metrics.height*0.5`. `DrawText` is then called with only the measured-size rect, guaranteeing pixel-perfect horizontal and vertical centering at any DPI. This restores the approach that was proven correct in the May 23 snapshot of `DX11Renderer.cpp`.
- *See: [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 GameMenu buttons not bold; font changed from MayaCulpa to Segoe UI** (`GUIWindows.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`, `Renderer.h`, `IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp`):
  GameMenu buttons (Configuration, Game Play, High Scores, Credits, Quit, Experimental) had `bold = true` only for OpenGL/Vulkan builds. Added `#elif defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)` branch setting `bold = true` at font size 16 for all six buttons. `DX12Renderer::DrawMyTextCentered` previously ignored the bold flag entirely (parameter was `bool /*bold*/`) because `MayaCulpa` font has no native bold face and DWrite synthesis crashed. Fix: dropped MayaCulpa engine-wide; changed `Renderer.h` global `FontName` from `L"MayaCulpa"` to `L"Segoe UI"` (Windows system UI font with full bold support). Activated the `bold` parameter in `DrawMyTextCentered` and use `DWRITE_FONT_WEIGHT_BOLD` when true. Also updated the two commented-out `CreateTextScrollerConsistent` calls in `IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp` to use Segoe UI for consistency.
- *See: [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`Renderer.h`](Renderer.h), [`IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp`](IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 models invisible (shared Texture pixel cache cleared after first upload)** (`DX12Models.cpp`, `Models.h`):
  The `UploadDX12TextureToGPU` loop in `SetupModelForRendering` called `ClearDX12Pixels()` after uploading each texture. For shared `Texture` objects (e.g. the static fallback `bricks1.png` used by every model that has no diffuse texture, and combined metallic-roughness maps), the pixel cache was cleared on model 1's setup. Every subsequent model that shared the same `Texture` found `GetDX12Pixels().empty() == true`, skipped the upload, and ended up with a null SRV → all-black sampling → models invisible against the black clear colour. Fix: added `ComPtr<ID3D12Resource> m_dx12Resource` to the `Texture` class with `GetDX12Resource()` accessor. The upload loop now checks `GetDX12Resource()` first; if the texture was already uploaded by any earlier model, the cached `ID3D12Resource` is reused directly. After a successful upload the resource is stored in the `Texture`. `ClearDX12Pixels()` is called only after a successful upload (staging memory freed; GPU resource now lives in the Texture). Back-face culling was confirmed NOT the cause — the PSO already has `D3D12_CULL_MODE_NONE`.
- *See: [`DX12Models.cpp`](DX12Models.cpp), [`Models.h`](Models.h)*

- **Fix — DX12 models display brick fallback texture instead of correct diffuse texture** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  In `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel()`, the two `push_back` calls that register a GLTF `baseColorTexture` image into `textureSRVs` / `normalMapSRVs` were guarded by `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_11__)` only — missing `|| defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)`. Every other texture type in the same function (explicit normal map, metallic-roughness ORM, AO, solid-colour fallback) already had the correct combined guard. Because `textureSRVs` stayed empty in DX12 for models with real image textures, `SetupModelForRendering` (DX12Models.cpp:403) detected `textureSRVs.empty()`, called `LoadFallbackTexture()`, and uploaded `Assets/bricks1.png` as the sole diffuse texture. Both `SCENE_GAMEPLAY` (brick visible on all models) and `SCENE_GAMETITLE` (fallback colours) were caused by this same omission. Fix: changed both guards to `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_11__) || defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)`, matching the rest of the function. `SceneManager` is the authority for all pipeline model setup; `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel` must populate `textureSRVs`/`normalMapSRVs` correctly for all renderers before `SetupModelForRendering` is called.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Diagnostic — `_DEBUG_SCENEMANAGER_` logging added to texture load path** (`SceneManager.cpp`, `DX12Models.cpp`):
  `LoadGLTFImage` and `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel` now emit detailed `_DEBUG_SCENEMANAGER_` log messages at each texture load decision point: the resolved full path with `exists=YES/NO`, a `LoadFromFile FAILED` message distinguishing "bad path" from "device/WIC error", per-texture `LoadGLTFImage returned NULL` messages naming the URI and image index, a `CreateSolidColorTexture FAILED` message if the fallback itself fails, and failure logs for MetallicRoughness, Normal Map, and AO map loads. Additionally `DX12Models.cpp LoadFromFile` now logs `GetFrame`, `CreateFormatConverter`, `Initialize`, `GetSize`, and `CopyPixels` failure HRESULTs so the exact WIC failure step is visible in any build.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp), [`DX12Models.cpp`](DX12Models.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — FBXImporter debug gating and comprehensive parse diagnostics** (`FBXImport.cpp`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  All `LOG_INFO` and `LOG_WARNING` messages in `FBXImport.cpp` are now gated under `#if defined(_DEBUG_FBXIMPORTER_)` — they are completely silent in non-debug builds. Only `LOG_ERROR` and above (genuine failures) are always emitted. The former `LOG_WARNING` "No 'Objects' node found" was promoted to `LOG_ERROR` as it represents a malformed file.
  Comprehensive step-by-step diagnostics added throughout the FBX pipeline, all guarded by `_DEBUG_FBXIMPORTER_`:
  - **Binary header:** version, offset width (32/64-bit), and file size logged at parse start.
  - **Top-level nodes:** every successfully-parsed root node name, child count, and property count is logged as each node enters `ParseBinary`.
  - **Corrupt records:** `ParseBinaryNode` now logs the node name, the oversized `endOffset`, and the actual file size in the corrupt-record/property-count warnings (previously these were anonymous messages with no context).
  - **GlobalSettings:** `upAxis`, `frontAxis`, `coordAxis` (with sign), and `unitScaleFactor` logged after extraction.
  - **ExtractObjects:** entry count logged; unhandled object types named.
  - **ExtractGeometry:** name, id, raw-position count, PVI count, normals, UVs, tangents, and material-index count logged per geometry; mapping/reference type strings included.
  - **ExtractModel:** name, type, id, parentID, geometryID, material count, and full TRS (translation, rotation Euler, scale) logged per model.
  - **ExtractMaterial:** name, id, shading model, diffuse colour, metalness, roughness, opacity, and texture IDs logged per material.
  - **ProcessConnections:** total connection record count logged before resolution begins.
  - **TriangulateGeometry:** pre-pass logs raw-position count, PVI count, polygon count, estimated triangle count, and which attribute layers are present (normals/UVs/tangents) with their mapping types. Post-pass logs output vertex and index counts, triangle count, and the full axis-aligned bounding box (min/max/centre) of the triangulated mesh.
  - **BuildMaterial:** per-material logs diffuse colour, metalness, roughness, opacity, and whether each texture slot was resolved or absent.
  **SceneManager diagnostics** (`_DEBUG_SCENEMANAGER_`): `ParseFBXScene` now logs the FBX GlobalSettings summary (upAxis, unitScaleFactor, totals) immediately after `LoadFile`. For every model slot, the local translation (post-coord-flip), scale, and resulting world-matrix position are logged, making it straightforward to identify scale or placement issues.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX compressed array decompression fails for all arrays (`InflateData`)** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  `InflateData` used the Windows Compression API (`COMPRESS_ALGORITHM_MSZIP | COMPRESS_RAW`) to decompress FBX property arrays. MSZIP operates on 32 KB chunked blocks; standard zlib (as emitted by Blender, Maya, and other FBX exporters) produces a continuous RFC 1951 DEFLATE stream. The two formats are incompatible, so every `Decompress()` call returned a size-mismatch or hard failure, producing 18+ "InflateData: Decompress failed or size mismatch" log errors and leaving all geometry arrays empty. Also fixed: `bool` array element size was computed as 4 bytes instead of the correct 1 byte, causing `plainLen` to be 4x too large for any compressed boolean array. Fix: removed the Windows Compression API call entirely and replaced `InflateData` with a self-contained inline DEFLATE inflate (RFC 1951). The implementation lives in an anonymous namespace in `FBXImport.cpp` and covers all three DEFLATE block types: stored (type 0), fixed Huffman (type 1), and dynamic Huffman (type 2), with correct length/distance extra-bit tables. No external library is required.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — `OpenMovieAndPlay()` called twice on scene transition to `SCENE_INTRO_MOVIE`** (`main.cpp`):
  When `RENDERER_IS_THREAD` is defined (always on, set in `Renderer.h`), the `FadeOutThenCallback` lambda at the end of `SCENE_INTRO` already performs the complete scene transition: `InitiateScene`, `FadeToImage`, `OpenMovieAndPlay`, and `ResumeLoader`. However, the main loop also checked `if (scene.bSceneSwitching && !fxManager.IsFadeActive())` guarded only by `#if !defined(__USE_OPENGL__)`. For DX11 (and DX12), this guard did not fire, so after the fade completed the main loop called `SwitchToMovieIntro()` → `OpenMovieAndPlay()` a second time. The result was every DX11 initialisation inside `OpenMovie` (D3D11 multithreaded protection, URL processing, D3D manager setup, BGRA texture creation) executing twice, and the video being opened and started twice. Fix: extended the preprocessor guard to `#if !defined(__USE_OPENGL__) && !defined(RENDERER_IS_THREAD)`, matching the existing OpenGL exclusion rationale.
- *See: [`main.cpp`](main.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — Debug log file cleared at session start** (`Debug.h`, `Debug.cpp`):
  Previously the log file was opened with `OPEN_ALWAYS | FILE_APPEND_DATA` on every write, so successive application runs accumulated entries from prior sessions in `DebugLog.txt`, making it difficult to isolate output from the current run. Added a `Debug()` constructor (the global `Debug debug;` instance lives in `main.cpp` and is constructed before `WinMain` runs, so the clear happens before any thread or logging call is active). The constructor calls the new private `static void ClearLogFile(const std::wstring& filename)` helper, which is guarded by `#if !defined(NO_DEBUGFILE_OUTPUT)` so it is a complete no-op when file logging is disabled. Platform guards inside `ClearLogFile` select the correct OS API: on Windows (`#if defined(_WIN32) || defined(_WIN64)`) `CreateFileW` with `CREATE_ALWAYS` + `GENERIC_WRITE` is used — this atomically truncates an existing file or creates a new one; on POSIX systems `std::ofstream` with `std::ios::trunc` is used as the fallback. Because the constructor runs before any other thread exists, no mutex is required for the truncation itself. The existing per-write `s_logMutex` in `Insert_Into_Log_File` remains unchanged and continues to serialise all subsequent log writes.
- *See: [`Debug.h`](Debug.h), [`Debug.cpp`](Debug.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX binary parser crash: `abort()` via `std::bad_alloc` on corrupt node header** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  Stack trace (SIGABRT, thread 13532): `ParseBinaryNode` (FBXImport.cpp:487) → `vector<FBXProperty>::reserve` → `operator new` → `NewHandler` (ExceptionHandler.cpp:765) → `std::bad_alloc` → `terminate` → `abort`. A corrupt or malformed binary FBX file can contain a `numProps` or `endOffset` value far larger than the file size. `ParseBinaryNode` was calling `out.properties.reserve(numProps)` with the raw file-sourced value without any bounds validation, causing a multi-gigabyte heap allocation request that failed and triggered the custom new-handler chain. Three guards added immediately before `reserve()`: (1) `endOffset > data.size()` — rejects nodes whose claimed end offset exceeds the file; (2) `propsEnd > data.size()` — rejects nodes whose property block would extend past the end of the file; (3) `numProps > propListLen` — rejects a corrupted `numProps` (impossible in a valid file since each property is at minimum 1 byte, so `numProps` can never exceed `propListLen`). All three conditions emit a `LOG_WARNING` and return `false`. No changes to the happy path.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — Binary FBX root loop incorrectly continues past null sentinel into opaque footer** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  The root node loop in `ParseBinary` used `if (off == savedOff) break; continue;` when `ParseBinaryNode` returned false. This caused the loop to re-enter after the null sentinel advanced `off` by 13 bytes, then attempt to parse the opaque 160-byte FBX footer as a valid node. Because the footer's first 4 bytes form a plausible `endOffset` value larger than the file, the corrupt-record guard fired and emitted the spurious WARNING `node '÷&~' endOffset=162249978 exceeds fileSize=42644972`. Fix: changed the root loop to `if (!ParseBinaryNode(...)) break;` — consistent with how `ParseBinaryNode` itself handles child-list iteration. The null sentinel is the correct end-of-list marker; no valid nodes can follow it at the root level.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Diagnostic — `ProcessConnections` geometry/material link debug logs** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  Added `_DEBUG_FBXIMPORTER_`-gated log messages when `ProcessConnections` resolves a geometry→model or material→model `OO` connection. Each log prints the source FBX ID, the target model name, and the slot index, making it immediately visible whether the connection wiring succeeded (geometryID resolved, material linked) or was silently skipped due to a missing map entry.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Diagnostic — `ParseFBXScene()` emits WARNING when Mesh model has no resolved geometry** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  After `ProcessConnections`, each model marked `type=Mesh` is checked with `isMesh = (geom != nullptr && !geom->polygonVertexIndex.empty())`. If `isMesh` is false (geometry link missing), the model was silently treated as a transform-only node and `SetupModelForRendering()` was never called, leaving the model invisible with no log output. Added an unconditional `LOG_WARNING` at this decision point that prints the model name, the raw `geomID` value, whether `geom` was found in the geometry map, and the PVI count. This makes the root cause of "model not rendering" immediately diagnosable from the log.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX model slot search changed to name-based lookup** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  The slot search in `ParseFBXScene` previously used `!m_isLoaded && !bInitialized` to find an empty `models[]` slot. When `cache.dat` was loaded via `LoadCache()`, all slots it populated had `m_isLoaded = true` and `bInitialized = true`, so the search found no match and either reused the wrong slot or logged "models[] pool exhausted". Fixed by replacing the flag-based search with the same name-based pattern used by `ParseGLBScene`: first scan for a slot whose `name` and `sourceSceneFile` match the FBX model being instantiated (cache hit), then fall back to the first slot with an empty name (fresh slot). This correctly re-uses existing cache slots on scene revisits and integrates with `cache.dat` restoration.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — FBX in-memory cache fast-path in `ParseFBXScene()`** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  On second and subsequent visits to the same FBX scene (or after `LoadCache()` restores `models[]` from `cache.dat`), the engine previously re-parsed the entire FBX file and re-called `SetupModelForRendering()` regardless of whether GPU resources were already present. Added a cache fast-path at the top of `ParseFBXScene` (mirroring `ParseGLBScene`) that scans `models[]` for entries with `sourceSceneFile == fbxFile` and `bGpuReady == true`. If any are found, `scene_models[]` is restored directly from those slots: GPU buffers and materials are copied, GPU-buffer validity is checked per-renderer (DX11/DX12/Vulkan/OpenGL) and `SetupModelForRendering` is called only when buffers are absent, vertex data is re-applied from `models[m]` if `scene_models[idx].vertices` is empty, and all TRS/animation fields are restored. Sets `bLoadedFromCache = true` and returns early without touching the FBX file.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — Author attribution and critical function-level comments added to `FBXImport.h` / `FBXImport.cpp`** (`FBXImport.h`, `FBXImport.cpp`):
  Both files now carry a top-level author block: "Originally created by Daniel J. Hobson, Melbourne, Australia 2026." Critical comments added to all major functions in `FBXImport.cpp` explaining purpose, algorithm, and non-obvious implementation details: `InflateData` (inline DEFLATE, zlib header skip); `ParseBinaryProperty` (type-code table, array 12-byte header, encoding==1 DEFLATE); `ParseBinaryNode` (node layout, sentinel end-of-list signal); `TriangulateGeometry` (bitwise-NOT end-of-polygon, fan triangulation, layer mapping modes); `BuildMaterial` (texture ID path resolution); `ConvertAnimations` (FBX time unit, AnimStack walk, Euler-to-quaternion pipeline). `EulerToMatrix` updated with extrinsic-convention comment. `BuildTransformMatrix` updated with full FBX SDK transform order description.
- *See: [`FBXImport.h`](FBXImport.h), [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — `EulerToMatrix` rotation order table corrected for FBX extrinsic convention** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  FBX defines rotation orders as extrinsic (each named axis is applied first to the fixed world frame). In DirectX row-vector convention the leftmost matrix is applied first, so extrinsic XYZ = `Rx * Ry * Rz`. Cases 1 (XZY), 2 (YXZ), 4 (ZXY), and 5 (ZYX) had incorrect products — e.g. case 1 XZY was `Rz * Ry * Rx` (ZYX order). Corrected to: `Rx * Rz * Ry` / `Ry * Rx * Rz` / `Rz * Rx * Ry` / `Rz * Ry * Rx`. Cases 0 (XYZ, Blender default) and 3 (YZX) were already correct and unchanged.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — `FBXImporter::ApplyRotationFlip()` — RH to LH rotation matrix conversion** (`FBXImport.h`, `FBXImport.cpp`):
  New public method converts a rotation matrix from FBX right-handed space to engine left-handed Y-up space via a similarity transform. Derivation: `R_LH = MT * R_RH * M` (row-vector), where M is the coordinate-mapping matrix. Y-up: M = diag(1,1,-1), self-inverse, gives `M * R * M`. Z-up: M_row maps (x,y,z)->(x,z,-y), MT = M^{-1} = transpose(M), gives `MT * R * M`. Net effect on Y-up rotations: Rx(θ)->Rx(-θ), Ry(θ)->Ry(-θ), Rz(θ)->Rz(θ) — X and Y rotations flip sign; Z rotation is preserved. Method is declared public so `SceneManager` can call it for both static TRS and animation keyframes.
- *See: [`FBXImport.h`](FBXImport.h), [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — `ConvertAnimations` rotation keyframes: apply `ApplyRotationFlip` and use per-model rotation order** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  Rotation keyframes were built with hard-coded order 0 (XYZ) and no RH->LH conversion. Two fixes: (1) rotation order is now looked up from the target model in `m_scene.modelByID` so non-XYZ exports animate correctly; (2) `ApplyRotationFlip(rot)` is called after `EulerToMatrix` and before `XMQuaternionRotationMatrix` so the extracted quaternion is in engine LH space.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — `ParseFBXScene` model TRS rotation converted to engine LH space** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  The rotation matrix from `EulerToMatrix` was passed directly to `XMQuaternionRotationMatrix` without coordinate-system conversion, producing an RH quaternion in an LH engine. Added `rotM = m_fbxImporter.ApplyRotationFlip(rotM)` between `EulerToMatrix` and the quaternion extraction. The world matrix reconstruction now uses the corrected quaternion, so model orientation in the engine matches the intended exported pose.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — `ParseFBXScene` light position and direction correctly converted to engine LH space** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  Light world position was taken directly from the raw `BuildTransformMatrix` result (FBX RH space); light direction was `XMVector3TransformNormal((0,0,-1), world_RH)` without flipping the result. Both are now converted: position receives the same axis flip as model translations (`Y-up: (x,y,-z)`; `Z-up: (x,z,-y)`); direction is obtained by transforming `(0,0,-1)` through the raw RH rotation and then applying the same coordinate flip to the resulting world-space vector.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Feature — FBX camera system: `ParseFBXCameras`, `GotoCamera`, `bCameraJumped`** (`SceneManager.h`, `SceneManager.cpp`, `DXCamera.h`, `IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp`):
  When an FBX file contains one or more cameras, the engine now extracts them, converts their position/target/up to engine LH space, and automatically applies the first camera to the engine's `Camera` instance at parse time. All parsed cameras are stored in `std::vector<ParsedFBXCamera> m_fbxCameras` (exposed read-only via `GetFBXCameras()`), cleared at the start of every new scene load so stale cameras never persist.
  - **`ParsedFBXCamera` struct** (`SceneManager.h`): stores `name`, `position`, `target`, `up`, `fovYDeg`, `nearPlane`, `farPlane` — all in engine LH space.
  - **`ParseFBXCameras(const FBXScene&)`** (`SceneManager.cpp`): iterates `fbx.cameras`; finds the owning model node by matching `attributeID` to `camera.id` and extracts its world position via `BuildTransformMatrix`; converts interestPos (target) and up vector to LH space; applies near/far from the FBX camera record; stores every camera in `m_fbxCameras`. Immediately applies the first camera: sets `cam.position`, `cam.target`, `cam.up`, calls `SetNearFarPlanes`, `SetFieldOfView`, `SetProjectionMatrix(XMMatrixPerspectiveFovLH)`, `SetViewMatrix(XMMatrixLookAtLH)`, and `SetYawPitchFromForward()`. Sets `cam.bCameraJumped = true` and `bGltfCameraParsed = true`.
  - **`bool GotoCamera(const std::wstring& cameraName, bool AnimateTowards)`** (`SceneManager.h`, `SceneManager.cpp`): returns `false` with `LOG_WARNING` if the named camera is not in `m_fbxCameras`. Always sets projection (FOV, near, far). `AnimateTowards=false`: instant jump — sets position, target, up, and calls `SetViewMatrix` + `SetYawPitchFromForward()`. `AnimateTowards=true`: sets target/up immediately, calls `cam.JumpTo(x, y, z, 2, true)` for a smooth animated transition. Sets `cam.bCameraJumped = true` in both cases. Returns `true` on success.
  - **`bool bCameraJumped = false`** (`DXCamera.h`): public `Camera` member. Set to `true` by `ParseFBXCameras` or `GotoCamera`. When `true`, the LoaderThread skips both `SetupDefaultCamera()` and `SetPosition()` overrides so the FBX camera position is preserved after scene load completes.
  - **LoaderThread guards** (`IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp`): both `SetupDefaultCamera` call sites and both `SetPosition` call sites are wrapped in `if (!myCamera.bCameraJumped)` so the default camera is never applied over a parsed FBX camera.
  - **Context:** `SplashShip1` was positioned at `lclT=(-485, 0, 145)` — far off screen — visible only from the FBX export camera. `GotoCamera` or automatic first-camera application frames it correctly without needing to manually set camera position.
- *See: [`SceneManager.h`](SceneManager.h), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp), [`DXCamera.h`](DXCamera.h), [`IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp`](IOStreamDX11Thread.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX `BuildMaterial` `loadTex`: unreliable load-success check allowed null SRVs through** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  `loadTex` used `std::make_shared<Texture>(path)` whose constructor calls `LoadFromFile` but ignores its `bool` return value. `LoadFromFile` sets `texturePath` before any load attempt, so `GetPath()` is always non-empty even when WIC decoding or `CreateShaderResourceView` fails. The old check `if (!tex->GetPath().empty()) return tex` therefore returned a `Texture` with a null SRV on load failure. That null SRV was pushed into `textureSRVs`, `SetupModelForRendering` saw a non-empty vector and skipped the fallback, and the renderer bound a null SRV at draw time. Fixed by using the default `Texture()` constructor and calling `LoadFromFile` explicitly so its return value can be checked; returns `nullptr` on failure, which causes `ParseFBXScene`'s solid-colour-from-`diffuseColor` path to fire instead. Added `_DEBUG_FBXIMPORTER_`-gated `LOG_WARNING` on failure. Policy enforced: (1) texture file loads OK → use texture; (2) texture missing/fails, material present → solid colour from `Kd`; (3) no material → brick fallback.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX materials not rendering: `textureSRVs` / SRV slots never populated in `ParseFBXScene`** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  Two bugs in the FBX material application block. (1) `textureSRVs`, `normalMapSRVs`, `roughnessMapSRV`, `metallicMapSRV`, and `aoMapSRV` were never populated — `Texture` shared_ptrs were added to `m_modelInfo.textures` but their raw SRVs were never pushed into the DX SRV vectors. `SetupModelForRendering` checks `textureSRVs.empty()` and applies the brick fallback when true, so FBX models always rendered with the brick texture regardless of their actual materials. Fixed by pushing each resolved texture's `GetSRV()` into the matching slot (same pattern as the GLTF load path). Added a solid-colour fallback from `fbxMat.diffuseColor + opacity` when no texture file resolves, preventing the brick fallback from ever firing. (2) Only `materialIDs[0]` was processed — a mesh with 48 materials had only the first built and registered. Fixed by looping all `materialIDs`: every material is built via `BuildMaterial` and stored in `m_materials` (ready for future per-material draw-call splitting); the first material alone populates the GPU SRV slots used by the current single-draw-call render path.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11 crash: SEH 0x80000003 (assert) in `XMMatrixPerspectiveFovLH` when applying FBX camera** (`DXCamera.cpp`):
  `ParseFBXCameras` called `cam.SetFieldOfView(fovYDeg)` after `SetNearFarPlanes`. Inside `SetFieldOfView`, `GetNearPlane()` and `GetFarPlane()` extract the near/far values from the projection matrix to preserve them. Both extraction functions used the **RH/OpenGL** formula (`_33 = -(far+near)/(far-near)`, `_43 = -2*far*near/(far-near)`) — but `XMMatrixPerspectiveFovLH` produces an **LH** matrix where `_33 = far/(far-near)` and `_43 = -far*near/(far-near)`. With these elements the old formula returned `GetNearPlane() = -far` (negative!). `XMMatrixPerspectiveFovLH` hard-asserts `NearZ > 0.0f`, triggering the SEH breakpoint `0x80000003`. Fixed by correcting both extraction formulas to the proper LH derivations: `near = -m43/m33`; `far = m43/(1-m33)`.
- *See: [`DXCamera.cpp`](DXCamera.cpp)*

#### June 08, 2026

- **Fix — Multi-material FBX mesh: geometry split into per-material sub-meshes** (`FBXImport.h`, `FBXImport.cpp`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  A joined FBX mesh with N materials (e.g. `RedHull` + `Material` using per-polygon `materialIndex`) was rendered as a single draw call using only the first material — all other polygons shared that material's colour, making the mesh visually incorrect. Root cause: `TriangulateGeometry` discarded per-polygon material indices, and `ParseFBXScene` had no mechanism to route triangles to per-material GPU sub-meshes.
  **`TriangulateGeometry` (`FBXImport.h` / `FBXImport.cpp`):** Added a fourth output parameter `std::vector<int32_t>& outTriMatIdx`. The fan-triangulation loop was converted from range-for to index-for so the polygon index `p` is available. For each output triangle the correct polygon material index is pushed: `materialMappingType == "ByPolygon"` → `materialIndex[p]`; `"AllSame"` → `materialIndex[0]`; no index array → 0. One entry is emitted per output triangle (not per vertex), matching `outIdx`'s triangle stride.
  **`ParseFBXScene` (`SceneManager.cpp`):** Replaced the single-mesh instantiation block with a per-material sub-mesh loop:
  1. Calls `TriangulateGeometry(*geom, verts, idx, triMatIdx)` with the new signature.
  2. Collects unique material slots from `triMatIdx` in first-appearance order; falls back to `{0}` for meshes with no material index data.
  3. For each unique slot: extracts only the triangles that belong to that slot into a compact `subVerts` / `subIdx` array (remapping vertex indices via a local hash map); finds or allocates `scene_models[]` and `models[]` slots; for sub-meshes beyond the first, a fresh `ModelInfo` is constructed that inherits world-transform and metadata from the base mesh but has a unique name (`<FBXModelName>_mat<N>`) and `iParentModelID` pointing to the first sub-mesh.
  4. Resolves the `FBXMaterial` for the slot's index; calls `BuildMaterial`; creates a solid-colour 1×1 diffuse texture from `fbxMat.diffuseColor + opacity` when no texture file is present; populates `textureSRVs` / `normalMapSRVs` / `roughnessMapSRV` / `metallicMapSRV` / `aoMapSRV` under the DX11/DX12 guard.
  5. Calls `SetupModelForRendering` and syncs GPU handles to `models[]` per the existing renderer-conditional pattern.
  6. The first sub-mesh's `scene_models[]` index is stored in `fbxIDToSlot[fbxModel.id]`; additional sub-meshes are extras that animate with the parent via `iParentModelID`. `instanceIndex` is incremented once per sub-mesh.
  Policy unchanged: texture file present and loads → use it; texture missing/fails and material present → solid colour from `Kd`; no material → brick fallback via `SetupModelForRendering`.
- *See: [`FBXImport.h`](FBXImport.h), [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — Normal map fallback removed: models without a normal map now use geometry vertex normals** (`ModelPixel.hlsl`, `Models.cpp`, `DX12Models.cpp`):
  `SetupModelForRendering` previously called `LoadFallbackNormalMap()` whenever `normalMapSRVs` was empty, creating a 1×1 flat-normal (0.5, 0.5, 1.0) texture for every model that had no normal map. Policy change: no fallback — models without a normal map render using geometry vertex normals with the material colour, not a synthesised flat texture.
  **Shader (`ModelPixel.hlsl`):** `NormalScale == 0` is the "no normal map" signal. The shader branches: when `NormalScale <= 0.0f` it sets `normalWS = N` (the vertex normal) directly; when `NormalScale > 0` it samples the normal map, decodes, and applies the TBN transform as before. T and B are only computed in the normal-map branch.
  **C++ render path (both DX11 and DX12):** (1) Removed `LoadFallbackNormalMap()` calls from `SetupModelForRendering` and per-frame render paths. (2) When `normalMapSRVs.empty()`, the `MaterialBuffer` update now forces `NormalScale = 0.0f` overriding any material-stored value, so the shader always takes the vertex-normal path for these models. (3) The normal map slot (t1) is now always explicitly set — bound to the SRV when present, bound to `null` when absent — preventing a stale SRV from a previously rendered model leaking into the next draw call.
- *See: [`Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.hlsl`](Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.hlsl), [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp), [`DX12Models.cpp`](DX12Models.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX material colour always white: `DiffuseColor` property name variant not handled** (`FBXImport.cpp`):
  `ExtractMaterial` called `ReadP70Vec3(*p70, "DiffuseColor", {1,1,1})` which returns the `{1,1,1}` white default when the property is not found. Blender (and some Maya versions) export the diffuse colour under the legacy alias `"Diffuse"` rather than the FBX 7.x standard name `"DiffuseColor"`. Because only one name was tried, both material colours (grey body + orange windows) resolved to white, causing the solid-colour 1×1 diffuse texture to be created with RGB=(1,1,1) regardless of what the FBX file contained.
  **Fixes applied to `ExtractMaterial`:**
  - `diffuseColor`: try `"DiffuseColor"` first; if not found (sentinel value -1), fall back to `"Diffuse"`. Apply `DiffuseFactor` multiplication and clamp to [0,1] (FBX spec: `actual_diffuse = DiffuseColor × DiffuseFactor`).
  - `ambientColor`: try `"AmbientColor"` then `"Ambient"`.
  - `specularColor`: try `"SpecularColor"` then `"Specular"`.
  - `emissiveColor`: try `"EmissiveColor"` then `"Emissive"`.
  - Added fallback `FindChild("Properties")` when `FindChild("Properties70")` returns null (FBX 6.x format compatibility).
  - Added unconditional `LOG_WARNING` when neither Properties70 nor Properties is present, to make this failure diagnosable without enabling `_DEBUG_FBXIMPORTER_`.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp)*

- **Fix — FBX and GLTF solid-colour diffuse texture double-apply darkened/whited materials** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  The shader multiplies the sampled diffuse texture by the material `Kd` constant buffer value (`albedoColor.rgb *= Kd`). When no texture file is present both the FBX sub-mesh path and the GLTF no-texture fallback path created a solid-colour 1×1 texture using the `Kd` / `diffuseColor` value — meaning the shader evaluated `Kd × Kd` rather than `Kd`. For typical linear diffuse values (0.05–0.5) this squared the colour toward near-black; for the prior-session white-default case (property name mismatch) both texture and Kd were `{1,1,1}` so the result was still white.
  **Fix:** both paths now create a `{1,1,1}` (white) 1×1 solid-colour texture. The actual material colour is carried exclusively by `Kd` in the material constant buffer; the shader evaluates `white × Kd = Kd`, producing the correct material colour with a single application.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp) — GLTF no-texture fallback ~line 3503; FBX sub-mesh solid-colour ~line 4865*

- **Fix — FBX geometry cache restore redesigned to match `ParseGLBScene` GLTF/GLB pattern** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  The FBX cache fast-path restored geometry from `models[]` but performed no texture rebind — SRVs and `shared_ptr<Texture>` objects do not survive a `cache.dat` reload or device reset, so models appeared invisible or with fallback brick textures after a session restore. The fast-path also emitted a single `LOG_INFO` with no per-model diagnostics.
  **New six-step pattern matching `ParseGLBScene`:**
  1. Re-parse the FBX file via `m_fbxImporter.LoadFile()` before touching `scene_models[]` — restores cameras (`ParseFBXCameras`), lights (inline loop), and material data.
  2. Restore `scene_models[]` geometry from the `models[]` pool; GPU rebuild is triggered if vertex/index/constant buffers are null (handles `cache.dat` restore and device reset).
  3. **Texture rebind** — for each cached model: clear stale SRVs, look up its FBX material by name in the freshly-parsed scene, call `BuildMaterial`, create a white 1×1 diffuse texture, push fresh SRVs into `textureSRVs` / `normalMapSRVs`, update `m_materials`, write back to `models[]` for subsequent reloads.
  4. Rebuild the FBX model ID → `scene_models[]` slot map (`cIDToSlot`) by matching FBX model names against cached names (first sub-mesh always retains the original FBX model name).
  5. Convert and log FBX animations via `ConvertAnimations(cIDToSlot, ...)`.
  6. Emit always-on `LOG_INFO` for every cache hit, every texture rebind (with resolved `Kd` values), and the final CACHE HIT summary — visible without recompiling with `_DEBUG_SCENEMANAGER_`.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp) — FBX cache fast-path ~line 4308*

- **Enhancement — Full conditional shader redesign: useDiffuseMap, gloss map, emissive texture, PCF shadow, tangent-W bitangent** (`ModelPixel.hlsl`, `ModelVertex.hlsl`, `ModelPixel.glsl`, `ModelVertex.glsl`, `ConstantBuffer.h`, `Includes.h`, `Models.h`, `ShaderManager.cpp`, `Models.cpp`, `DX12Models.cpp`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  The shader system has been fully redesigned to support conditional map paths and the complete GLTF feature set:
  **`useDiffuseMap` flag:** When 0 (solid-colour materials), the shader uses `float4(Kd, 1.0)` directly — no texture sample, no incorrect `Kd × Kd` double-apply. When 1 (real texture), `diffuseTexture.Sample(t0) × Kd`. Set during scene parsing in `SceneManager.cpp` for both GLTF and FBX paths.
  **Gloss map (t6):** New `SLOT_glossMap=6`, `useGlossMap` flag. When active: `roughness = 1.0 − glossMap.r`. Overrides both the base `Roughness` value and any roughness map at t3.
  **Emissive texture (t7):** New `SLOT_emissiveMap=7`, `useEmissiveMap` flag. When active: `emissive = EmissiveFactor × emissiveMap.Sample(t7).rgb × EmissiveStrength`. When inactive: existing constant-factor-only path unchanged.
  **PCF shadow map (t8):** New `SLOT_shadowMap=8`, `ShadowBuffer` cbuffer at `b6` (`ShadowBufferGPU`: `lightViewProj`, `shadowBias`, `shadowStrength`, `useShadowMap`, `shadowMapSize`), `SamplerComparisonState shadowSampler` at `s2` (`SLOT_SHADOW_SAMPLER_STATE=2`). `SampleShadow()` projects world-space position to light clip space, remaps UV, and runs a 3×3 PCF kernel via `SampleCmpLevelZero` (HLSL) / `sampler2DShadow` hardware PCF (GLSL). Shadow factor multiplies `directLighting` only; ambient and emissive are unaffected. `debugMode==7` now shows the actual shadow factor grey-scale instead of hardcoded black.
  **Fixed debug modes 3 and 4:** `ProcessLight()` was updated to take `out float3 outDiff, out float3 outSpec` parameters. The main loop accumulates `diffuseAccum` and `specularAccum` separately across all lights. `debugMode==3` (LightingOnly) now correctly returns `diffuseAccum`; `debugMode==4` (SpecularOnly) returns `specularAccum`. Previously both returned garbage from uninitialized accumulators.
  **Tangent-W bitangent (GLTF handedness):** `VS_INPUT.tangent` changed from `float3` to `float4` in both HLSL and GLSL vertex shaders. Bitangent corrected from `cross(T, N)` to `normalize(cross(N, T.xyz)) × T.w` per the GLTF 2.0 specification — fixes incorrect lighting on mirrored UV islands (e.g., symmetric ship hulls). `ShaderManager.cpp` input layout updated from `R32G32B32_FLOAT` to `R32G32B32A32_FLOAT` at offset 32. `Models.h` `Vertex` struct extended: `float tangentW = 1.0f` (DX11/DX12); `float tangent[4]` (OpenGL/Vulkan).
  **`MaterialGPU` pad fields reused:** `pad4/pad5/pad6` replaced by `useDiffuseMap/useGlossMap/useEmissiveMap`. Struct size unchanged at 112 bytes. New `ShadowBufferGPU` struct (80 bytes) added.
- *See: [`Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.hlsl`](Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.hlsl), [`Assets/Shaders/ModelVertex.hlsl`](Assets/Shaders/ModelVertex.hlsl), [`Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.glsl`](Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.glsl), [`Assets/Shaders/ModelVertex.glsl`](Assets/Shaders/ModelVertex.glsl), [`ConstantBuffer.h`](ConstantBuffer.h), [`Includes.h`](Includes.h), [`Models.h`](Models.h), [`ShaderManager.cpp`](ShaderManager.cpp), [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp), [`DX12Models.cpp`](DX12Models.cpp), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

#### June 11, 2026

- **Port — FBX Importer and new material fields cross-ported to DX12, Vulkan, and OpenGL pipelines** (`FBXImport.cpp`, `Includes.h`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`, `VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`, `Models.cpp`, `SceneManager.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderer.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderer.h`, `OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`):
  The FBX 7.x importer introduced in the previous commit used DX-specific vertex member types (`XMFLOAT3`, `XMFLOAT2`) throughout `ComputeTangents` and `TriangulateGeometry`, and the new material flags (`useDiffuseMap`, `useGlossMap`, `useEmissiveMap`) were wired only into the DX11 pipeline. This session completed the full cross-platform port and fixed the resulting Vulkan and OpenGL compilation failures.

  **`Includes.h` — renderer default guard fix:** The old `#ifndef __USE_VULKAN__ / #define __USE_VULKAN__` chain caused CMake OpenGL builds to activate both `__USE_OPENGL__` and `__USE_VULKAN__` simultaneously, breaking every `#if`/`#elif` renderer guard across the codebase. Replaced the five individual `#ifndef` blocks with a single `#if !defined(any_renderer) … #define __USE_VULKAN__` guard so the IDE default (Vulkan) only fires when cmake-build.bat has not already injected a renderer define.

  **`FBXImport.cpp` — cross-platform vertex field access:** `TriangulateGeometry` and `ComputeTangents` now guard all direct struct-member assignments with `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_11__) || defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)` / `#else` blocks. DX path uses `XMFLOAT3` members directly; OGL/Vulkan path uses the `float[]` array form. In `ComputeTangents`, the Gram–Schmidt orthogonalisation `t - n * dot(n, t)` extracts the dot product as a scalar via `XMVectorGetX` before the multiply — the stub `Vector4` has `operator*(float)` but not `operator*(Vector4)`, and `XMVectorGetX` works on both the stub and the real DX `__m128`.

  **`SceneManager.cpp` — FBX camera API guards:** `ParseFBXCameras` and `GotoCamera` wrapped DX-specific camera calls (`XMFLOAT3 position`, `SetProjectionMatrix(XMMATRIX)`, `bCameraJumped`) in `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_11__) || defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__)` / `#else glm` blocks, matching the existing pattern in `ParseGLTFCamera`.

  **`DX12Renderer.cpp` — text centering precision fix:** Ported the `IDWriteTextLayout`-based pixel-perfect centering from DX11 to `DrawMyTextCentered`; replaced `DWRITE_TEXT_ALIGNMENT_CENTER` with a layout-metrics approach that computes the exact centred origin from `DWRITE_TEXT_METRICS::width` / `height`.

  **`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp` — material UBO expansion and text fix:** Updated inline `k_glsl3DFrag` `MaterialUBO` from 64 to 80 bytes (added `useDiffuseMap`, `useGlossMap`, `useEmissiveMap`, `_pad` as the 5th std140 row); added gloss and emissive texture uniforms (`binding=4/5`) and their shader logic. Expanded `CreateDescriptorSetLayouts` from 4 to 6 sampler bindings and `CreateDescriptorPool` from 4096 to 6144 samplers. Ported `DrawMyTextCentered` precision fix using `m_d2dRenderTarget`.

  **`Models.cpp` — Vulkan material UBO and fallback textures:** Updated `SetupModelForRendering` Vulkan path: `matUboSize` 64→80, `MatUBO` struct with 3 new flag fields + `_pad`, fallback view array 4→6 (slots 4/5 reuse the default diffuse view for gloss/emissive).

  **`SceneManager.cpp` — Vulkan material writes:** Updated `VKMatUBO` struct to 80 bytes; added `useDiffuseMap`, `useGlossMap`, `useEmissiveMap` assignments; expanded `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel` texture descriptor writes from 4 to 6 (gloss and emissive views with white fallback).

  **`OpenGLRenderer.cpp` — inline shader gloss/emissive uniforms:** Added `uGlossMap`, `uEmissiveMap`, `uHasGlossMap`, `uHasEmissiveMap` uniforms to `k_3dFragGLSL`; gloss path derives `effectiveRoughness = 1.0 − glossMap.r`; emissive path samples `emissiveTex` when flag is set.

  **`OpenGLRenderer.h` / `OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp` — uniform caching and binding:** Added four new `GLint` fields to `CachedUniforms3D`; wired gloss (GL_TEXTURE6) and emissive (GL_TEXTURE7) binding in both `UploadModelUniformsCached` and `UploadModelUniformsDynamic`.

  All four pipelines (DX11, DX12, Vulkan, OpenGL) compile cleanly after these changes.
- *See: [`FBXImport.cpp`](FBXImport.cpp), [`Includes.h`](Includes.h), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp), [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderer.cpp`](OpenGLRenderer.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderer.h`](OpenGLRenderer.h), [`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`](OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12 `CreateGraphicsPipelineState` E_INVALIDARG crash on startup** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.h`):
  `CreatePipelineState()` was failing with `HRESULT 0x80070057` (E_INVALIDARG) at startup. Two rounds of fixes were required.

  **Pass 1 — TANGENT input layout:** PSO declared `TANGENT` as `DXGI_FORMAT_R32G32B32_FLOAT` (3 floats) but the vertex shader reads `float4 tangent : TANGENT` (4 components). Fixed to `DXGI_FORMAT_R32G32B32A32_FLOAT`. Also removed a bogus `BITANGENT` input element (shader computes bitangent from N×T; no vertex input needed).

  **Pass 2 — Root signature / sampler mismatch:** The pixel shader had been updated with PCF shadow mapping (`ShadowBuffer b6`, `shadowMap t8`, `SamplerComparisonState s2`) but the root signature was not updated to match. Three simultaneous issues:
  - **Static sampler s2 type mismatch (primary E_INVALIDARG cause):** s2 was `D3D12_FILTER_ANISOTROPIC` (non-comparison). The shader uses s2 as `SamplerComparisonState` with `SampleCmpLevelZero`. D3D12 validates sampler type at PSO creation → E_INVALIDARG. Fixed to `D3D12_FILTER_COMPARISON_MIN_MAG_LINEAR_MIP_POINT` / `LESS_EQUAL` / border white (lit outside shadow frustum).
  - **Missing b6 root parameter:** shader reads `cbuffer ShadowBuffer : register(b6)` but root sig had no b6. Added root parameter 7 = `InitAsConstantBufferView(6, ...)`.
  - **SRV table too small:** table covered t0–t5 only; shader now uses t0–t8 (+gloss t6, emissive t7, shadow depth t8). Expanded to 9 descriptors; null SRV pre-population expanded from 6 to 9 slots.

  Supporting changes: `m_shadowBuffer` (b6) allocated in `CreateConstantBuffers` with `useShadowMap=0` (shadows disabled until a shadow map is provided); bound in `PopulateCommandList`; `Reset()` added to cleanup. `DX12Renderer.h`: added `DX12_ROOT_PARAM_SHADOW_BUFFER = 7` constant and `m_shadowBuffer` member.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.h`](DX12Renderer.h)*

- **Fix — `ModelPixel.hlsl` FXC X4000 shader compiler warnings** (`ModelPixel.hlsl`):
  Two `warning X4000: use of potentially uninitialized variable` warnings were emitted by the FXC shader compiler.

  - **`ProcessLight` (line 203):** FXC's out-parameter dataflow analysis does not track that `outDiff` and `outSpec` are assigned unconditionally at the top of the function (before any branch). It warns at each early-return statement that the `out` parameters might be unset. Fix: removed both early returns (`light.active == 0` and `NdotL <= 0.0001`). Replaced with nested `[branch]` if-blocks so the function has a single `return outDiff + outSpec;` at the bottom — FXC can now prove all paths set the `out` params. Logic unchanged.
