It has been reformatted to `<BuildType> <Renderer> CPGE v<Major>.<Minor>.<Build> <dd-MM-YYYY>` where `<BuildType>` is `Debug` or `Release` (resolved at compile time via `#if defined(_DEBUG)`), `<Renderer>` is the existing `RENDERER_NAME_W` (e.g. `DirectX 12`), and `<dd-MM-YYYY>` is the actual build date derived from the compiler's `__DATE__` macro (e.g. `Debug DirectX 12 CPGE v0.0.1725 15-06-2026`). The build date is computed once per session via a static-local lambda that parses the `__DATE__` string into zero-padded `DD-MM-YYYY` format. `BUILD_TYPE_W` macro added to `Includes.h` (alongside the other identity macros) so it is never overwritten by the auto-generated `BuildInfo.h`.
- *See: [`Includes.h`](Includes.h), [`DXRenderFrame.cpp`](DXRenderFrame.cpp), [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp), [`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`](VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`](OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp)*

#### June 16, 2026

- **New Tool — `Python/ShipMaker.py` v2.0: Blender 5.0+ add-on for procedural sci-fi fighter ship generation as named component collections, with Geometry Nodes surface detail, PBR Image Texture nodes, animations, and dedicated Bake + Export operators** (`Python/ShipMaker.py`):
  Complete rewrite (v2.0) of the Ship Maker Blender add-on. Every ship is now built as a **Blender Collection** of individually named mesh objects so each component can be selected, modified, or retextured independently in the scene. Dedicated **Bake PBR Textures** and **Export All Ships FBX** buttons are separate from Generate and clearly visible in their own panel boxes. Full feature set:
  - **Named part objects per ship** — each ship collection contains: `Hull_Body`, `Nose_Cone`, `Cockpit`, `Wing_R`, `Wing_L`, `WingTip_R`, `WingTip_L`, `Fin_Dorsal`, `Thruster_R/L` (×2 or ×4), `ThrusterNozzle_R/L` (×2 or ×4), plus type-specific extras: `Sensor_Array` (Interceptor), `Armor_Cheek_R/L` (Heavy Fighter), `Gun_Barrels` (Assault Corvette).
  - **Full seed-driven geometry** — `make_params(seed)` generates every dimension value (hull length/width/height, nose length/segments, cockpit position/size, wing span/sweep/taper/dihedral/chord, wing-tip cant/height, fin height/sweep/taper, thruster radius/length/nozzle-flare, greeble count/depth, GN noise scale) from the seed so identical seeds always produce identical ships and different seeds produce visibly different designs.
  - **Geometry Nodes `ShipMaker_SurfaceDetail` modifier** applied to every part: noise texture sampled by surface position and displaced along the face normal; inputs `Noise Scale` and `Displacement` exposed in the modifier stack so users can tune detail per-part without touching the mesh.
  - **Three ship types selectable from UI**: Interceptor, Heavy Fighter, Assault Corvette, or Random.
  - **Three materials per ship**: Hull (Principled BSDF with procedural panel-lines, metallic ramp, roughness ramp, animatable Emission Strength, and **pre-wired Image Texture nodes** with Mix nodes for BaseColor / Roughness / Metallic / Normal — Mix Fac flips to 1.0 after baking to use maps), Glass (high-transmission canopy), Glow (emission nozzle, separately animatable `GlowStrength`).
  - **Three NLA animation actions** on hull body: `Idle` (emission pulse, material node tree, 60 fr looping), `Patrol` (gentle roll + yaw, object transforms, 120 fr looping), `Combat` (sharp banking roll, object transforms, 80 fr looping).
  - **`Bake PBR Textures` operator** — scans all `Ship_*` collections in the scene, bakes BaseColor, Roughness, Normal, and Metallic (Metallic via emission reroute pass) at chosen resolution (1024/2048/4096), saves PNGs to `Assets/textures/`, then wires images into hull material Image Texture nodes and sets Mix Fac to 1.0.
  - **`Export All Ships FBX` operator** — selects all objects in each `Ship_*` collection and exports each as a separate FBX 7.4 binary file to the Assets folder with all NLA animation strips baked.
  - **UI panel** (`View3D > Ship Maker` tab) with three clearly labelled boxes: Ship Generation (Count, Seed, Type, Generate button), PBR Texture Baking (resolution selector, Bake button), FBX Export (Export button).
- *See: [`Python/ShipMaker.py`](Python/ShipMaker.py)*

- **New — `assembly.asm` / `assembly.h`: x86/64 MASM optimisation module wired into both MSVS2022 and CMake build systems**:
  Establishes the engine's assembly optimisation layer using Microsoft Macro Assembler (MASM / ml64.exe) for x86-64. Both build systems updated to assemble `assembly.asm` automatically alongside the C++ sources.
  - **`assembly.asm`** — MASM x64 source file using the Windows x64 calling convention (RCX/RDX/R8 for first three args; RSI/RDI saved/restored as callee-saved non-volatile registers). Contains the first optimised routine:
    - **`MemoryCopy(Source, Destination, Length)`** — fast memory copy via `REP MOVSQ` (8 bytes per clock, hardware-bandwidth throughput on modern Intel/AMD) followed by `REP MOVSB` for the 0-7 trailing byte remainder. Source and Destination must not overlap.
  - **`assembly.h`** — C++ header with `extern "C"` declarations for all MASM routines so the MSVC linker matches undecorated labels and C++ callers can include the header directly.
  - **`CMakeLists.txt`** — `enable_language(ASM_MASM)` added inside `if(MSVC AND WIN32)` guard (before `add_executable`); `assembly.asm` conditionally appended to `SOURCES` via `list(APPEND)` so non-Windows / non-MSVC platforms are unaffected.
  - **`CrossPlatformGameEngine.vcxproj`** — `ExtensionSettings` now imports `$(VCTargetsPath)\BuildCustomizations\masm.props`; `ExtensionTargets` now imports `masm.targets`; new `<MASM Include="assembly.asm" />` ItemGroup added; `assembly.h` added to ClInclude.
- *See: [`assembly.asm`](assembly.asm), [`assembly.h`](assembly.h), [`CMakeLists.txt`](CMakeLists.txt), [`CrossPlatformGameEngine.vcxproj`](CrossPlatformGameEngine.vcxproj)*

- **Fix — `CMakeLists.txt`: MASM A4018 warnings eliminated by guarding all MSVC CL flags with `$<COMPILE_LANGUAGE:CXX>`**:
  CMake's `target_compile_options()` was broadcasting every C++ flag (`/wd4244`, `/Zc:__cplusplus`, `/MP`, `/MDd`, `/sdl`, `/FS`, etc.) to `ml64.exe`, which does not understand them. Fixed by wrapping every CL-only flag in `$<$<COMPILE_LANGUAGE:CXX>:...>` and config+language combined guards; ml64.exe now only receives `/nologo` via `$<$<COMPILE_LANGUAGE:ASM_MASM>:/nologo>`.
- *See: [`CMakeLists.txt`](CMakeLists.txt)*

- **Fix — `VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`: Vulkan fallback descriptor set (`m_defaultTexSetDescSet`) expanded from 4 to 6 bindings** (`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`, `VULKAN_Renderer.h`, `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`):
  `m_3dTexSetLayout` declares six combined-image-sampler bindings (0=diffuse, 1=normal, 2=ORM, 3=AO, 4=gloss, 5=emissive), but the global fallback set `m_defaultTexSetDescSet` only wrote four `VkWriteDescriptorSet` entries — bindings 4 (gloss) and 5 (emissive) were undefined, causing Vulkan validation errors whenever the fallback set was bound for models without their own `textureDescriptorSet`. Fixed by expanding the loop to write all six bindings using `m_defaultTexture.view` (1×1 white) as the fallback for slots 4 and 5; the fragment shader samples these only when `useGlossMap > 0.5` / `useEmissiveMap > 0.5`, so the white fallback is silent. The stale `// 4-slot fallback set` comment in `VULKAN_Renderer.h` and the matching comment in `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp` were updated to reflect the corrected 6-slot layout.
- *See: [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.h`](VULKAN_Renderer.h), [`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`](VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — `AnimateLights()` now called consistently across all four render pipelines** (`DXRenderFrame.cpp`, `DX12RenderFrame.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`):
  `LightsManager::AnimateLights(deltaTime)` (Pulse / Flicker / Strobe / None modes) was only invoked in `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`; the DX11, DX12, and OpenGL render frames read light data via `GetAllLights()` / `UpdateConstantBuffers()` without first advancing the animation state, so animated lights were static on those three pipelines. Added `lightsManager.AnimateLights(deltaTime)` in each missing render frame, placed immediately before the light-data upload so animated intensity and colour values are baked into the per-frame GPU upload:
  - **DX11** (`DXRenderFrame.cpp`) — before the `PSSetConstantBuffers(SLOT_GLOBAL_LIGHT_BUFFER, ...)` global light upload block.
  - **DX12** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`) — before `UpdateConstantBuffers()` (which calls `GetAllLights()` inside `DX12Renderer.cpp`).
  - **OpenGL** (`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`) — before `lightsManager.GetAllLights()` and the `glBufferSubData` GlobalLightBuffer UBO upload.
- *See: [`DXRenderFrame.cpp`](DXRenderFrame.cpp), [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`](OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — `Lights.cpp`: `AnimateLights()` `None` mode no longer overwrites `intensity` with `baseIntensity`** (`Lights.cpp`):
  `LightsManager::AnimateLights()` contained a `case LightAnimMode::None: light.intensity = light.baseIntensity;` branch that ran every frame regardless of whether any animation was active. In the gameplay scene the sun light is configured as `intensity = 0.5f`, `baseIntensity = 0.1f`; once `AnimateLights()` was added to the DX11 / DX12 / OpenGL render paths, the `None` branch silently clamped intensity from `0.5` down to `0.1` on every frame, making all models appear almost completely dark. Fixed by replacing the `None` case with a no-op `break` — when no animation is active, `intensity` is authoritative and must not be overwritten; `baseIntensity` is used exclusively by the Pulse / Flicker / Strobe modes as their animation baseline.
- *See: [`Lights.cpp`](Lights.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — `Lights.h`: Per-renderer light consumption reference block with conditional guards** (`Lights.h`):
  Added a clearly documented `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_11__) || defined(__USE_DIRECTX_12__) / #elif defined(__USE_OPENGL__) / #elif defined(__USE_VULKAN__)` guard block between the struct definitions and the `Light` class declaration. The block documents exactly how `LightStruct` / `LightBuffer` / `GlobalLightBuffer` reach the GPU on each pipeline (DX11: `PSSetConstantBuffers` b1/b3; DX12: `Map/Unmap` upload heap + `SetGraphicsRootConstantBufferView`; OpenGL: `glBufferSubData` + `glBindBufferBase` at `GLSL_BINDING_GLOBAL_LIGHT` (3); Vulkan: 32-byte push-constant `VKLightPC` via `vkCmdPushConstants`, `GlobalLightBuffer` not uploaded) and notes where `AnimateLights(dt)` must be called relative to the upload on each path.
- *See: [`Lights.h`](Lights.h)*

- **Fix — Vulkan materials and textures now correctly applied to GLTF models** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  GLTF models rendered with flat untextured surfaces on the Vulkan pipeline despite DX11 and DX12 working correctly. Root cause: `SetupModelForRendering()` creates the material UBO and texture descriptor set (set=1) filled with defaults (`useDiffuseMap = 0`, all 6 image views pointing to the 1×1 white fallback). The subsequent `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel()` call in the Vulkan second-bind block was intended to overwrite those defaults with the real GLTF material data — but because it called `LoadGLTFImage()` a second time on an already-decoded texture, the reload produced inconsistent results and left `useDiffuseMap` at zero, so the fragment shader never sampled the diffuse texture, rendering everything as flat grey. Fixed in both GLTF scene load paths (first-scene and second-scene) by replacing the redundant `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel()` call with `UploadFBXMaterialToVulkanModel()`, which uses the `Material` objects already resident in `scene_models[instanceIndex].m_materials` (populated by the first bind pass inside `LoadGLTFMeshPrimitives()` and carried through `CopyFrom()`). These `Material` objects already hold valid `VkImageView` handles from the first upload, so no second disk read or GPU decode is needed. A fallback to `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel()` is retained for the rare case where `m_materials` is empty. Additionally, `UploadFBXMaterialToVulkanModel()` was extended to support GLTF gloss and emissive maps: the previously hardcoded `useGlossMap = 0.0f` / `useEmissiveMap = 0.0f` lines now read `info.useGlossMap` / `info.useEmissiveMap`, and the gloss/emissive descriptor-set slots are resolved from `mat.glossMap` / `mat.emissiveMap` instead of always falling back to the default white view. FBX models are unaffected — their `useGlossMap` / `useEmissiveMap` flags remain `false` by default and their `glossMap` / `emissiveMap` pointers remain null, so the fallback logic is identical to before.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **New — `MoviePlayer::Reset()`: full MF/audio teardown and reinitialize with Windows/Linux/macOS platform guards** (`MoviePlayer.cpp`, `MoviePlayer.h`):
  Adds a `Reset()` public method so that when a video finishes playing the caller can restore the player to a clean initialized state without destroying and recreating the object. The method acquires `m_mutex`, calls the existing `Cleanup()` to release every MF COM object, DirectX texture, and XAudio2 voice and to call `MFShutdown()`; then resets variables not zeroed by `Cleanup()` (`m_llCurrentPosition`, `m_audioReadPosition`, `m_firstAudioSamplePTS`, `m_audioStartSamples`, `m_samplesPlayedOffset`, `m_cpuFrameBuffer`, `m_cpuFrameWidth/Height`, `m_videoSubtype`); and finally calls `InitializeMF()` and, if audio was enabled, `InitializeAudio()` to restore the engine to a fully initialized state ready for the next `OpenMovie()` call. `m_renderer`, `m_threadManager`, `m_enableAudio`, and `m_targetFPS` are preserved across the reset. The method is wrapped in `#if defined(_WIN32) / #elif defined(__linux__) / #elif defined(__APPLE__)` platform guards, with GStreamer and AVFoundation stubs (returning `false` with a log message) ready for future Linux and macOS implementations.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp), [`MoviePlayer.h`](MoviePlayer.h)*

- **Optimisation — All 4 renderer pipelines: `memcpy`/`memset` hot paths replaced with x86/64 assembly routines** (`assembly.asm`, `assembly.h`, `Includes.h`, `DXRenderFrame.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`, `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`):
  Extended the engine's MASM assembly optimisation layer with two new routines and replaced every per-frame `memcpy`/`memset` hot path across all four render pipelines with direct assembly calls.
  - **`MemoryZero(Destination, Length)`** — new MASM routine using `REP STOSQ` (8 zero bytes per clock) + `REP STOSB` for 0-7 trailing bytes; equivalent to `memset(dst, 0, n)` at hardware memory bandwidth. Replaces the GPU mapped-region zero-pass before `GlobalLightBuffer` upload in DX11 `RenderGamePlay`.
  - **`MatrixCopy4x4F(Source, Destination)`** — new MASM leaf routine (no push/pop) using four 128-bit `MOVUPS` loads + four `MOVUPS` stores to copy the exact 64-byte footprint of a 4×4 float matrix without loop or division overhead. `XMM0–XMM3` are caller-saved in the Windows x64 ABI so this is a zero-overhead leaf call. Used for world/view/projection matrix uploads in `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`.
  - **`assembly.h`** — declarations for `MemoryZero` and `MatrixCopy4x4F` added alongside the existing `MemoryCopy` `extern "C"` block.
  - **`Includes.h`** — `#include "assembly.h"` added at file end inside `#if defined(_WIN64)` guard so all translation units pick up the declarations automatically on Windows x64 with no per-file include needed.
  - **MASM `IFDEF` conditional assembly** — `assembly.asm` now contains documented `IFDEF PLATFORM_WINDOWS`, `IFDEF __USE_DIRECTX_11__`, `IFDEF __USE_DIRECTX_12__`, `IFDEF __USE_OPENGL__`, `IFDEF __USE_VULKAN__` guard sections. Defines must be passed to `ml64.exe` via `/D` flags (see comment block in `assembly.asm` for the `set_source_files_properties` CMake snippet). On Windows all four renderer IFDEFs are active simultaneously because the engine compiles all backends and selects at runtime.
  - **DX11 `RenderGamePlay`** (`DXRenderFrame.cpp`): camera constant buffer upload `memcpy` → `MemoryCopy`; per-element `for` light-copy loop replaced by single bulk `MemoryCopy(globalLights.data(), glb.lights, numLights * sizeof(LightStruct))`; GPU region zero `memset` → `MemoryZero`; global-light-buffer GPU upload `memcpy` → `MemoryCopy`.
  - **OpenGL `RenderGamePlay`** (`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`): per-element `for` light-copy loop replaced by single bulk `MemoryCopy` on `_WIN64`; non-Windows platforms retain `memcpy` inside the `#else` branch.
  - **Vulkan `RenderGamePlay`** (`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`, Windows path): world/view/projection matrix uploads (64 bytes each) replaced with `MatrixCopy4x4F`; full 224-byte `VKCameraUBO` upload to mapped GPU memory replaced with `MemoryCopy`; all wrapped in `#if defined(PLATFORM_WINDOWS)` / `#else std::memcpy` guards so Linux/Android retain `std::memcpy` unchanged.
- *See: [`assembly.asm`](assembly.asm), [`assembly.h`](assembly.h), [`Includes.h`](Includes.h), [`DXRenderFrame.cpp`](DXRenderFrame.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`](OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp), [`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`](VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: TSOO image now composites on top of 3D models; fireworks correctly render beneath 3D models** (`DXRenderFrame.cpp`):
  The DX11 render pipeline executes in three ordered D2D/D3D passes: `RenderBackgroundImage()` (pre-3D D2D pass) → `RenderGamePlay()` (D3D 3D model rendering) → 2D overlay D2D pass. Previously, the TSOO image blit (`BlitObj2DIndexType::IMG_TSOO`) was issued inside `RenderBackgroundImage()` for `SCENE_GAMETITLE`, meaning it composited *before* all 3D model draw calls — placing the logo image beneath spinning ship models. Fixed by removing the TSOO blit from `RenderBackgroundImage()` and adding it to the 2D overlay `SCENE_GAMETITLE` case (inside the post-`RenderGamePlay()` D2D `BeginDraw/EndDraw` block), so the logo now renders on top of all 3D geometry. A `bLoaderTaskFinished` + null-texture guard was added at the new call site to match the safety conditions of the original location. Fireworks (`fxManager.RenderFireworks()`) are unchanged — they remain in `RenderBackgroundImage()` and therefore continue to render behind 3D models as intended.
- *See: [`DXRenderFrame.cpp`](DXRenderFrame.cpp)*

#### June 17, 2026

- **Fix — Vulkan: 3D models now render (descriptorSet no longer nulled before texture rebind)** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  All Vulkan models rendered as nothing — the draw guard in `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp` (`descriptorSet != VK_NULL_HANDLE && vertexBuffer != VK_NULL_HANDLE && ...`) always failed. Root cause: the Vulkan pre-rebind cleanup block in SceneManager cache-restore Step 4 (and the matching GLB fresh-load rebind path) set `scene_models[ti].m_modelInfo.descriptorSet = VK_NULL_HANDLE` immediately before calling `BindGLTFMaterialTexturesToModel()`. That function only rebuilds `textureDescriptorSet` (set=1, texture image bindings); it never re-allocates `descriptorSet` (set=0, which holds the transform UBO + material UBO + shadow UBO bindings allocated in `SetupModelForRendering()`). After the call, `descriptorSet` remained `VK_NULL_HANDLE` permanently, and the draw guard rejected every model every frame. Fixed by removing the two `descriptorSet = VK_NULL_HANDLE` assignments (at the GLTF cache-restore path and the fresh-load rebind path); `textures.clear()` is kept because that is the correct pre-rebind cleanup for the Vulkan texture vector.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: models no longer 2× too bright (global lights were double-counted via b1 and b3)** (`Models.cpp`):
  DX11 models appeared significantly over-lit compared to the DX12 reference build. Root cause: `ApplyDefaultLightingFromManager()` filled `m_modelInfo.localLights` with every global scene light; `UpdateModelLighting()` then uploaded those to `cbuffer b1` (`SLOT_LIGHT_BUFFER`) at draw time. `DXRenderFrame.cpp` also independently uploads all global lights to `cbuffer b3` (`SLOT_GLOBAL_LIGHT_BUFFER`) each frame. The `ModelPixel.hlsl` shader accumulates b1 and b3 into the same `directLighting` variable, so each global light was processed twice — producing 2× the intended brightness. DX12 was unaffected because `UpdateModelLighting()` is a no-op for non-DX11 builds (b1 is never populated). Fixed by adding a `#if defined(__USE_DIRECTX_11__) return;` early-exit at the top of `ApplyDefaultLightingFromManager()` so DX11 models always have empty `localLights`; b3 alone carries all scene lighting, matching DX12 behaviour exactly.
- *See: [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan & OpenGL: models over-lit compared to DX12 (double gamma correction)** (`Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.frag`, `ModelPixel.glsl`, `Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.glsl`):
  Vulkan and OpenGL 3D models appeared significantly brighter than the DX12 reference. Root cause: the Vulkan swap chain uses `VK_FORMAT_B8G8R8A8_SRGB` which applies automatic hardware gamma correction (sRGB encoding) on every pixel written to the framebuffer. `ModelPixel.frag` also manually applied Reinhard tone mapping followed by `pow(color, 1/2.2)` gamma — producing double gamma correction and an over-bright output. `ModelPixel.glsl` (OpenGL) had the same manual Reinhard + gamma pass. The DX12/HLSL shader (`ModelPixel.hlsl`) outputs linear colour directly with no tone mapping or gamma, matching the display pipeline. Fixed by removing the Reinhard tone-map and `pow(1/2.2)` lines from both GLSL shaders; both now output linear values and rely on hardware/display for gamma.
- *See: [`Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.frag`](Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.frag), [`ModelPixel.glsl`](ModelPixel.glsl), [`Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.glsl`](Assets/Shaders/ModelPixel.glsl)*

- **Fix — Vulkan: Fireworks now render before 3D models and before TSOO blit** (`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`):
  Fireworks were visually composited on top of 3D models (wrong order). Root cause: `m_drawToBackground` was set to `false` before calling `fxManager.RenderFireworks()` inside the background overlay block. `RenderFireworks()` uses `Blit2DColoredPixel`-style calls that check `m_drawToBackground` to select the render target; with the flag false they wrote to the main overlay (composited after 3D geometry). Fixed by moving `m_drawToBackground = false` to after `fxManager.RenderFireworks()`, so fireworks pixels land in the background overlay (composited before 3D models) and are ordered before the TSOO blit.
- *See: [`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`](VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan: `vkDeviceWaitIdle` threading error on scene transition** (`Models.cpp`, `VULKAN_FXManager.cpp`):
  Two `THREADING ERROR` validation warnings appeared on every scene transition: `vkDeviceWaitIdle(): object of type VkQueue is simultaneously used in current thread N and thread M`. Root cause: `Model::DestroyModel()` and `VKFXManager::DestroyFadePipeline()` called `vkDeviceWaitIdle(device)` directly. `vkDeviceWaitIdle` internally accesses all device queues; if the render thread simultaneously holds `m_queueMutex` during `vkQueueSubmit` or `vkQueuePresentKHR`, Vulkan validation detects the unsynchronised concurrent access. Fixed by replacing both bare `vkDeviceWaitIdle` calls with `vkr->WaitForGPUToFinish()`, which serialises the wait behind `m_queueMutex` — exactly matching the mutex guard already used around submit and present.
- *See: [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp), [`VULKAN_FXManager.cpp`](VULKAN_FXManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — WM_CLOSE now performs a proper graceful shutdown (no more hang on window close)** (`main.cpp`):
  Closing the window via the title-bar X button or Alt+F4 left the application hanging indefinitely. Root cause: no `WM_CLOSE` handler existed — Windows fell through to `DefWindowProc` → `DestroyWindow` → `WM_DESTROY` → `PostQuitMessage`, exiting the main loop without ever setting `bIsShuttingDown`. The renderer and loader threads therefore kept running during cleanup; `Cleanup()` blocked waiting for them to finish and the process never exited. Fixed by adding a `WM_CLOSE` handler that mirrors the ESC-key path (`KBHandlersCode.cpp`): calls `StopMusicPlayback()`, sets `threadManager.threadVars.bIsShuttingDown = true`, then calls `DestroyWindow(hwnd)` to continue the normal Windows destroy chain into `WM_DESTROY` → `PostQuitMessage`.
- *See: [`main.cpp`](main.cpp)*

- **Fix — ScreenRecorder no longer activates when Home key pressed outside the application window (all pipelines)** (`KBHandlersCode.cpp`):
  The screen recorder was activating when the Home key was pressed while another application or the desktop had focus, and this was also causing system instability / shutdowns. Root cause: the `WH_KEYBOARD_LL` low-level hook (Windows) and the macOS `CGEventTap` are system-wide; they fire for every key press regardless of which window is active. The `KEY_HOME` handler set `bRecordingToggleRequested = true` unconditionally, so the main loop would start the recorder — initialising WASAPI loopback capture and the MF H.264 encoder — even when the game was not the foreground window. Starting the heavy MF pipeline from a background state can corrupt MF resource state and cause system shutdowns. Fixed by adding a `GetForegroundWindow() == hwnd` guard (Windows) around the `bRecordingToggleRequested.store(true)` call inside the `KEY_HOME` case in `KBHandlersCode.cpp`. The guard is compiled only on `PLATFORM_WINDOWS` via a preprocessor block; non-Windows platforms retain the unconditional path (where the screen recorder is not implemented anyway). An `extern HWND hwnd` declaration was added at the top of the file inside a `PLATFORM_WINDOWS` guard. The fix applies identically to DX11, DX12, Vulkan, and OpenGL pipelines since the keyboard handler is shared.
- *See: [`KBHandlersCode.cpp`](KBHandlersCode.cpp)*

- **Fix — SCENE_INTRO → SCENE_INTRO_MOVIE: video now starts immediately; DX11 crash on transition fixed (all pipelines)** (`MoviePlayer.cpp`, `main.cpp`):
  A large delay was visible between the CPGE splash movie ending and the game intro movie appearing. Two root causes: (1) A redundant `moviePlayer.Stop()` + `moviePlayer.Reset()` in `main.cpp` was performing a full `MFShutdown()` + `MFStartup()` + XAudio2 engine recreation before every `OpenMovieAndPlay()` call — adding hundreds of milliseconds of stall. (2) `fxManager.FadeToImage(3.0f, ...)` covered the already-playing video for a full 3 seconds, making it appear as though the player was stalled. Fixed by replacing the conditional `Cleanup()` guard in `OpenMovie()` with an unconditional, lightweight per-file resource release (reader, sample, media type, source voice, DirectX/DX12 textures) that leaves the MF session and XAudio2 engine/mastering voice intact. The DX11 texture release is wrapped in `DX11Renderer::GetRenderMutex()` — the same mutex held by `UpdateVideoTexture()` and `Render()` while they access `m_videoTexture` — so the render thread cannot be mid-frame when the textures are freed (fixes a D3D11 SDK-layers exception 0x87D crash that occurred on transition without this guard). The explicit `Stop()`/`Reset()` calls in the `SCENE_INTRO` handler are removed. `FadeToImage` duration shortened from `3.0f` to `0.5f` in both `SwitchToMovieIntro()` and the inline `SCENE_INTRO` handler, and `OpenMovieAndPlay()` is moved before `FadeToImage()` in `SwitchToMovieIntro()` so the file is decoded as the brief fade-in plays. Fix applies to all render pipelines.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp), [`main.cpp`](main.cpp)*

#### June 18, 2026

- **Analysis & Fix — DX12 pipeline FPS below 60fps (37fps on title screen)** (`DX12FXManager.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  Three compounding root causes diagnosed. (1) **Double `UpdateStarfield` per frame**: `Render(true)` in the step-3.5 background pre-pass updated all 80 starfield particles, then `Render()` in the post-3D overlay pass iterated them again with dt≈0 — pure wasted work. `RemoveCompletedEffects()` (with its `ThreadLockHelper` acquisition) also ran twice. Fixed by guarding the update loop and cleanup call with `if (backgroundOnly)` / `if (!backgroundOnly)` respectively in `FXManager::Render()`. (2) **Per-pixel overhead in `Blit2DColoredPixel`**: Called 280+ times per frame (80 starfield stars + up to ~200 fireworks particles), each call was executing `IsDX11CompatibilityAvailable()` (3-pointer check), `threadManager.threadVars.bIsResizing.load()` (atomic read), and a try/catch wrapper — all redundant because `RenderFrame()` guards these conditions before any FX rendering starts. The try/catch is also dead weight since D2D `FillRectangle` never throws C++ exceptions. Removed all three from the hot path; only a fast null check on `m_d2dContext`/`m_pixelBrush` remains. (3) **Invisible particle waste**: Fireworks particles and starfield stars fade quadratically toward zero alpha. Added `alpha < 0.02f` early-continue guards in `DrawFireworksPixels` and `RenderStarfield` to skip D2D `FillRectangle` calls for nearly-invisible particles. The root architectural cause (two full D2D sessions per frame via 11on12 — one for the step-3.5 background pre-pass, one for the post-3D overlay — vs. one session in all other pipelines) remains an open item for a future pass; its fix requires compositing 3D content over a single D2D surface.
- *See: [`DX12FXManager.cpp`](DX12FXManager.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX12: Fireworks now render before 3D models and before TSOO blit** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`):
  Fireworks were composited on top of the 3D ship model (wrong visual order). Root cause: `fxManager.RenderFireworks()` was called inside the STEP 10 post-3D D2D pass (after the 3D command list had already executed), so fireworks pixels painted over the ship. Fixed by moving `RenderFireworks()` into the STEP 3.5 background pre-pass D2D block — after the starfield `fxManager.Render(true)` call and before `EndDraw()`. The pre-pass runs on the same D2D context before the 3D command list is re-opened, so the composition order is now: BACKGROUND → LOGO → STARFIELD → FIREWORKS → 3D MODELS → TSOO blit. The call was removed from STEP 10's `bBackgroundPrePassDone` branch to avoid rendering twice. Pipeline header comment updated to document the new order.
- *See: [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Optimisation — DX12 render pipeline** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`):
  Four targeted per-frame optimisations applied to `RenderFrame` and `RenderGamePlay`:
  (1) **Camera matrix hoisting** — `GetViewMatrix()`, `GetProjectionMatrix()`, and `GetPosition()` were called once per loaded model inside the `RenderGamePlay` loop; hoisted to single reads before the loop, reducing getter invocations from N×3 to 3 per frame.
  (2) **FPS timer deduplication** — the FPS counter called `steady_clock::now()` independently each frame; replaced with the per-frame `now` timestamp already captured for delta-time, eliminating a redundant syscall. The dead `lastFrameTimeFPS` static variable (set but never read in elapsed-time calculations) was removed.
  (3) **FPS text buffer** — the debug FPS overlay built its display string by chaining ~10 `std::to_wstring()` calls producing ~10 heap allocations per frame; replaced with a single fixed `wchar_t[512]` stack buffer formatted via `swprintf_s`, reducing this to zero heap allocations.
  (4) **Atomic load caching** — `threadManager.threadVars.bLoaderTaskFinished.load()` was called four times inside the D2D `BeginDraw` block each frame; cached as `const bool bLoaderDone` immediately after `BeginDraw()`, reducing four atomic reads to one (safe because this flag only ever transitions false → true).
- *See: [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: `cpge.mp4` intro movie crash at startup (`D3D11_3SDKLayers.dll` SEH exception `0x87D`)** (`MoviePlayer.cpp`):
  The DX11 debug validation layer raised an unhandled SEH exception (`0x0000087D`) on the very first rendered frame of intro-movie playback, crashing the engine inside `D3D11_3SDKLayers.dll` → `RaiseException`. Root cause (proven from stack trace and source): in `UpdateVideoTexture()`, `GeneratePlaceholderFrame()`, and `ProcessVideoSample()`, `ID3D11DeviceContext::CopyResource()` was called **while the staging texture (`m_videoTexture`) was still mapped** — the `Unmap()` call appeared after `CopyResource()` in all three functions. The D3D11 spec explicitly forbids any use of a mapped subresource as a `CopyResource` source or destination; the SDK validation layer enforces this by raising a fatal structured exception. Two additional violations in `GeneratePlaceholderFrame()` and `ProcessVideoSample()`: `D3D11_MAP_WRITE_DISCARD` was used on a `D3D11_USAGE_STAGING` texture — that map flag is only valid for `D3D11_USAGE_DYNAMIC` textures; the validation layer also throws for this. Fixed by: (1) moving `context->Unmap()` and `buffer->Unlock()` to **before** `CopyResource()` in all three functions so the staging texture is fully unmapped before the GPU copy begins; (2) changing `D3D11_MAP_WRITE_DISCARD` → `D3D11_MAP_WRITE` in `GeneratePlaceholderFrame()` and `ProcessVideoSample()`.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: `MoviePlayer::UpdateFrame` access violation (`0xC0000005`) on movie transition** (`MoviePlayer.cpp`):
  The render thread crashed with an access violation inside `MoviePlayer::UpdateFrame` when the loader thread called `OpenMovie()` to start the next video file. Root cause: `OpenMovie()` released `m_pCurrentSample`, `m_pSourceReader`, and `m_pSourceVoice` (COM objects) without acquiring `m_mutex`, while the render thread was simultaneously inside `UpdateFrame()` (which holds `m_mutex` via `try_to_lock`) accessing those same objects. The render thread followed a vtable pointer on a freed COM object, landing at a garbage code address and triggering an access violation. Fixed by wrapping the entire per-file teardown block in `OpenMovie()` (state flags, audio voice, MF COM objects, D3D textures, per-file scalars) with `std::lock_guard<std::recursive_mutex> teardownLock(m_mutex)`. When `OpenMovie()` holds `m_mutex`, the render thread's `try_to_lock` in `UpdateFrame()` fails immediately and the frame is skipped safely. Lock ordering (m_mutex → DX11 GetRenderMutex) is consistent with `UpdateVideoTexture()`, so no deadlock is introduced.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp)*

- **Fix — OpenGL: Render order — TSOO image, 3D models, fireworks, and starfield now composite correctly** (`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`):
  Three layering bugs corrected to match the DX11 pipeline. (1) `fxManager.RenderFireworks()` was never called in the OpenGL render loop — fireworks now render after the starfield pass and before `RenderGamePlay()`, so firework pixels appear behind 3D geometry. (2) The TSOO image was absent from the OpenGL 2D overlay section for `SCENE_GAMETITLE`; it is now blitted after `RenderGamePlay()` (centred, 536×466) so it composites on top of all 3D model and starfield rendering, matching DX11. (3) `fxManager.RenderLoadingText()` was gated on `!bLoaderTaskFinished`, preventing graceful fade-outs from completing after loading; it is now called unconditionally (no-op when no active effects), mirroring DX11 behavior.
- *See: [`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`](OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Fix — OpenGL: ZoomInOut effect no longer jumpy / pixelated** (`OpenGLRenderer.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderer.h`):
  The zoom animation on the OpenGL pipeline stuttered visibly compared to all other renderers. Root cause: `Blit2DCenteredZoom()` computed the centre-crop source rectangle in floating-point but then cast `srcX`, `srcY`, `srcW`, and `srcH` to integers before passing them to `Render2DQuad()`. That function divided these integer values by the texture dimensions to obtain UV coordinates, causing the UV sample window to jump discretely by ±1 pixel every few frames rather than gliding continuously — producing the blocky, jumping appearance. Fixed by adding `Render2DQuadUV()`, a private helper that accepts pre-computed normalised float UV coordinates and bypasses the integer conversion entirely. `Blit2DCenteredZoom()` now computes `u0/v0/u1/v1` directly from float arithmetic and calls `Render2DQuadUV()`, giving sub-pixel-accurate UV transitions and perfectly smooth zoom motion at all speeds.
- *See: [`OpenGLRenderer.cpp`](OpenGLRenderer.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderer.h`](OpenGLRenderer.h)*

- **Fix — DX11 (all pipelines): SCENE_GAMETITLE models no longer render black / unlit** (`Lights.h`, `Lights.cpp`, `SceneManager.h`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  The ship model in `SCENE_GAMETITLE` rendered completely dark — no lighting at all — even though `Sunlight` should illuminate it. Root cause (two separate bugs): (1) `splash-hover1.gltf` contains no `KHR_lights_punctual` extension, so `ParseGLTFLights()` returned `false` immediately and created zero lights in `lightsManager`. (2) `lightsManager` has no `ClearLights()` mechanism, meaning lights from a prior scene's parse accumulated and were never removed on scene transition — so if `SCENE_GAMETITLE` loaded first the map was empty, and if it followed another scene the map held stale foreign lights. With `globalLightCount == 0` the HLSL shader hit the no-lights early-exit branch in `ModelPixel.hlsl` (`if (numLights == 0 && globalLightCount == 0)`) and output only `Ka * albedo * AO` material ambient — producing black models. Fixed by: (a) Adding `ClearLights()` to `LightsManager` (clears the internal `lightMap` under mutex), called at the start of `ParseGLBScene()`, `ParseGLTFScene()`, and `ParseFBXScene()` so no prior-scene lights ever bleed into a new scene; (b) Adding `SceneManager::EnsureDefaultSunLight()`, called immediately after every lights-parse step (all 4 GLTF/GLB call sites and both FBX paths) — if `lightsManager.GetLightCount() == 0` it injects a single directional `DefaultSun` (warm-white, intensity 1.5, soft ambient 0.25, direction upper-left-front) so scenes with no embedded lights always receive meaningful illumination.
- *See: [`Lights.h`](Lights.h), [`Lights.cpp`](Lights.cpp), [`SceneManager.h`](SceneManager.h), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: `Model::Render()` aligned to DX12 11on12 reference for correct texture/material pipeline** (`Models.cpp`):
  Texture mapping and materials were not rendering correctly on the DX11 pipeline. Four structural divergences from the DX12 11on12 `Model::Render()` reference were found and corrected: (1) Shader binding now happens **before** `UpdateConstantBuffer()` — matching the DX12 11on12 ordering so the context is shader-ready before any Map/Unmap call. (2) `PSSetConstantBuffers(SLOT_MATERIAL_BUFFER)` is now **inside** the `if (SUCCEEDED(hr))` block — matching DX12 11on12; b4 is only bound when the buffer actually contains fresh material data for this frame (previously it was bound even if Map failed, with stale data). (3) Added an early null-guard for `vertexBuffer`, `indexBuffer`, and `constantBuffer` — matching DX12 11on12's guard that prevents any D3D11 calls from proceeding if GPU buffers are not yet fully initialised. (4) `LoadFallbackNormalMap()` is now called once in `SetupModelForRendering()` (matching DX12 11on12's setup-time fallback) so t1 always has a valid flat-normal SRV from first frame; the redundant per-frame call in `Render()` is removed.
- *See: [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: MoviePlayer SEH exception `0x87D` regression — `context->Map()` inside D2D `BeginDraw`** (`DXRenderFrame.cpp`, `MoviePlayer.cpp`, `DX11Renderer.cpp`, `DX11Renderer.h`):
  The D3D11 debug validation layer (`D3D11_3SDKLayers.dll`) raised SEH exception `0x87D` during `RenderFrame`, crashing the engine during intro-movie playback. The exception code `0x87D` is specifically raised by the debug layer when `ID3D11DeviceContext::Map()` or `CopyResource()` is called between a D2D `BeginDraw()` and `EndDraw()` — a hard constraint of the D2D/D3D11 interop layer. Root cause: `RenderIntroMovie()` (called from the main D2D render block, inside `BeginDraw`) called `moviePlayer.UpdateFrame()`, which internally calls `UpdateVideoTexture()` → `context->Map(m_videoTexture, D3D11_MAP_WRITE)` and `context->CopyResource()`. `Render()` then called `DrawVideoFrame()` → `context->Map(m_videoTexture, D3D11_MAP_READ)`. Both D3D11 context calls were made while D2D `BeginDraw` was still active, violating the interop contract and causing the debug layer to throw. Fixed by a two-part change: (1) `moviePlayer.UpdateFrame()` is moved out of `RenderIntroMovie()` and into `RenderFrame()` immediately before the D2D `BeginDraw` block — all D3D11 `Map/Unmap/CopyResource` calls in `UpdateVideoTexture()` and `GeneratePlaceholderFrame()` now execute outside `BeginDraw`. (2) `UpdateVideoTexture()` and `GeneratePlaceholderFrame()` now populate `m_cpuFrameBuffer` with the decoded BGRA frame while the staging texture is still mapped; a new `DX11Renderer::DrawVideoFrameFromCPU()` method reads from this CPU buffer and updates the D2D bitmap via `CopyFromMemory()` — a pure D2D call that is safe inside `BeginDraw`. `MoviePlayer::Render()` (DX11 path) is updated to call `DrawVideoFrameFromCPU()` instead of `DrawVideoFrame()`, eliminating all D3D11 context calls from the D2D render block.
- *See: [`DXRenderFrame.cpp`](DXRenderFrame.cpp), [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp), [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp), [`DX11Renderer.h`](DX11Renderer.h)*

- **Fix — DX11: SEH `0x87D` "same time" crash — `SetMultithreadProtected(TRUE)` deferred to `OpenMovie()` instead of device creation** (`DX11Renderer.cpp`):
  Root cause of the second `0x87D` crash: `ID3D10Multithread::SetMultithreadProtected(TRUE)` was only called inside `MoviePlayer::OpenMovie()`, but the D3D11 immediate context is accessed from both the render thread and the loader thread starting at `SCENE_INTRO` — long before any movie opens. The loader thread calls `LoadAllKnownTextures()` → `LoadTexture()` → `m_d2dRenderTarget->CreateBitmapFromWicBitmap()` (D2D uses D3D11 internally). Concurrently, the render thread uses `m_d3dContext` for 3D rendering. With `SetMultithreadProtected` not yet enabled, the D3D11 debug layer (`D3D11_3SDKLayers.dll`) detects both threads accessing the immediate context simultaneously and raises SEH `0x87D` with a "same time" message (fragments visible as `0x6D697420656D6173` / `0x207369680000001C` on the call stack). The D2D factory is `D2D1_FACTORY_TYPE_MULTI_THREADED` (which serialises D2D-internal calls) but this does not cover raw D3D11 context operations made from the loader or render threads outside of D2D — hence the debug layer violation. Fix: moved the `ID3D10Multithread::SetMultithreadProtected(TRUE)` call to immediately after `D3D11CreateDevice()` in `CreateDeviceAndSwapChain()`, so it is active before any loader thread activity and before any render thread–loader thread concurrent use.
- *See: [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — DX11: red material renders as blue (BGRA/RGBA channel swap in WIC texture load)** (`Models.cpp`):
  The DX11 pipeline showed the ship's red material panels as blue; all other pipelines (OpenGL, DX12, Vulkan) displayed red correctly. Root cause: the DX11 texture loading path converted the WIC frame to `GUID_WICPixelFormat32bppBGRA` (byte order B,G,R,A) but created the D3D11 texture with `DXGI_FORMAT_R8G8B8A8_UNORM` — the GPU read byte 0 (blue data) as red and byte 2 (red data) as blue, swapping the two channels entirely. Every other texture loading path in the file (lines covering the alternate WIC path, Vulkan path, etc.) correctly uses `GUID_WICPixelFormat32bppRGBA`. Fixed by changing `GUID_WICPixelFormat32bppBGRA` to `GUID_WICPixelFormat32bppRGBA` in the DX11 converter `Initialize()` call so the byte order matches `DXGI_FORMAT_R8G8B8A8_UNORM`.
- *See: [`Models.cpp`](Models.cpp)*

- **Fix — Vulkan: models render too bright / washed-out white (double gamma correction)** (`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`):
  Vulkan 3D models appeared significantly brighter and more white than the OpenGL reference — dark metal-gray surfaces rendered almost white. Root cause: the inline `k_glsl3DFrag` shader (runtime-compiled via shaderc and used for the `m_3dPipeline`) applied Reinhard tone mapping (`color = color / (color + vec3(1.0))`) followed by manual gamma encoding (`color = pow(color, 1/2.2)`) before writing to the framebuffer. The Vulkan swapchain format is `VK_FORMAT_B8G8R8A8_SRGB`, which applies hardware sRGB gamma encoding automatically on every pixel written — the stored value already undergoes `≈ pow(x, 1/2.2)`. With the shader also applying the same gamma, the stored pixel became `pow(pow(linear, 1/2.2), 1/2.2) = linear^(1/4.84)` — far too bright. The external `ModelPixel.frag` (correct reference) already outputs linear values with no tone mapping for exactly this reason. Fixed by removing both the Reinhard tone-map and the `pow(1/2.2)` lines from `k_glsl3DFrag`; the shader now outputs linear colour directly and relies on the sRGB swapchain for gamma, matching the DX12/OpenGL reference.
- *See: [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp)*

- **Fix — MoviePlayer audio crackling at high framerates (all pipelines)** (`MoviePlayer.h`, `MoviePlayer.cpp`):
  Audio crackled intermittently during movie playback when the engine ran above 30 fps. Root cause: `AUDIO_MAX_QUEUED_BUFFERS = 3` capped the XAudio2 buffer queue at 3 entries, and `kMaxAudioAheadMF = 5000000LL` (500 ms) limited how far audio was pre-filled ahead of video. At higher framerates the render loop calls `UpdateFrame()` more frequently but in shorter bursts; if all 3 slots were consumed before the next refill cycle arrived, XAudio2 momentarily starved and produced crackling. Fixed by raising `AUDIO_MAX_QUEUED_BUFFERS` from 3 to 8 and `kMaxAudioAheadMF` from 500 ms to 1000 ms (10000000LL), giving XAudio2 a larger pre-filled buffer pool that comfortably spans frame-time jitter at any framerate.
- *See: [`MoviePlayer.h`](MoviePlayer.h), [`MoviePlayer.cpp`](MoviePlayer.cpp)*

- **Optimisation — DX12: SCENE_GAMETITLE from 40-45fps to 60fps** (`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`, `DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  `SCENE_GAMETITLE` ran at 40-45fps in the DX12 pipeline while all other scenes hit 60fps. Five root causes found and fixed:
  (1) **Deferred inter-pass `dx11Context->Flush()`** — the `Flush()` after the STEP 3.5 D2D pre-pass stalled the CPU waiting for 11On12 to submit its internal command list to the shared hardware queue. Moved to immediately before `ExecuteCommandList()` at STEP 9; the CPU now records all 3D geometry commands while the GPU concurrently processes the pre-pass PRESENT→RENDER_TARGET transition and RTV clear — overlapping CPU recording with GPU execution.
  (2) **Removed redundant DSV clear from STEP 3.5 pre-pass** — the depth-stencil view was cleared twice per frame on SCENE_GAMETITLE: once in the pre-pass (STEP 3.5) and again unconditionally in STEP 6. No geometry writes depth between these two points, so the pre-pass clear was wasted GPU work. STEP 6 now performs the sole DSV clear.
  (3) **Renderer info string cached as `static const`** — `riText` was rebuilt every frame via 6+ `std::wstring` concatenations and `std::to_wstring()` calls (all heap-allocating), even though every component (`BUILD_TYPE_W`, `RENDERER_NAME_W`, `GAME_NAME_W`, version integers, and the already-static `buildDate`) is a compile-time constant or runtime-invariant value. Marked `static const` so the string is built once on first frame and zero-alloc thereafter.
  (4) **OSD timer deduplication** — the debug OSD elapsed-time check called `steady_clock::now()` independently; replaced with the per-frame `now` timestamp already captured at the top of the frame.
  (5) **Assembly bulk copies in `UpdateConstantBuffers`** — the per-light `memcpy` loop was replaced with a single `MemoryCopy(globalLights.data(), glb.lights, N * sizeof(LightStruct))` bulk transfer; `memset`/`memcpy` on the mapped GPU light buffer replaced with `MemoryZero`/`MemoryCopy` (REP STOSQ / REP MOVSQ); the ConstantBuffer upload replaced with `MemoryCopy`. In `RenderGamePlay`, the per-model `viewMatrix` and `projectionMatrix` assignments replaced with `MatrixCopy4x4F` (4 SSE MOVUPS loads+stores per matrix).
  Also: `DX12Renderer::RenderBackgroundImage()` was dead code — its entire D2D pass was superseded by the STEP 3.5 pre-pass and it was never called from within the DX12 render frame. Replaced with a no-op stub to retain the class declaration without any runtime overhead.
- *See: [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp), [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **Regression fix — DX12: `Blit2DColoredPixel` null brush; starfield and fireworks restored** (`DX12Renderer.cpp`):
  Starfield and fireworks particles stopped rendering entirely after the previous session's optimization pass. Root cause: `Blit2DColoredPixel` originally used a lazy `CreateSolidColorBrush` call inside itself — the only creation site for `m_pixelBrush`. The optimization stripped this call along with `IsDX11CompatibilityAvailable()`, `bIsResizing.load()`, and the try/catch wrapper, leaving `m_pixelBrush` permanently null. The existing null check (`if (!m_d2dContext || !m_pixelBrush) return;`) then caused every call to return immediately, silently discarding all pixel draws. The full original function is restored: on first call, `CreateSolidColorBrush` creates the member brush; on subsequent calls, `SetColor` updates its colour. All guards and the try/catch are retained as they serve genuine purposes in the DX12+11on12 interop path.
- *See: [`DX12Renderer.cpp`](DX12Renderer.cpp)*

- **Build — version stamp updated to v0.1.1790** (`BuildInfo.h`, `Version.id`):
  `CURRENT_BUILD_SUBVERSION` incremented from 0 to 1 and `CURRENT_BUILD` incremented from 1786 to 1790. `Version.id` updated to reflect `Current Build Version: v0.1.1790`. `GameConfig.cfg`'s stored `buildSubVersion: 0` will be auto-corrected to 1 on the next settings save (Configuration.cpp lines 117-120 always stamp `CURRENT_BUILD_SUBVERSION` after checksum validation).
- *See: [`BuildInfo.h`](BuildInfo.h), [`Version.id`](Version.id)*

- **Enhancement — Build scripts now own version identity: auto-increment `Version.id` and `BuildInfo.h` on every build** (`cmake-build.bat`, `Linux/cmake-build.sh`):
  `Version.id` and `BuildInfo.h` are now the exclusive responsibility of the build scripts; no other tool modifies them. At the start of each single-renderer build, PowerShell (`cmake-build.bat`) / Python 3 (`cmake-build.sh`) reads `Version.id` (`Current Build Version: vMAJOR.MINOR.BUILD`), increments the build number by 1, and writes the new value back to both files. `BuildInfo.h` is updated via regex so `CURRENT_BUILD_VERSION`, `CURRENT_BUILD_SUBVERSION`, and `CURRENT_BUILD` stay in sync. When `cmake-build all` is used the increment happens exactly once (for the first pipeline); subsequent pipelines skip it via the existing `SKIP_VERSION_INCREMENT` flag, so all four renderers share the same build number per invocation. The build aborts with a clear error if `Version.id` cannot be parsed.
- *See: [`cmake-build.bat`](cmake-build.bat), [`Linux/cmake-build.sh`](Linux/cmake-build.sh)*

- **Enhancement — ESC navigates back to Game Menu from GamePlayTypes / Difficulty windows in SCENE_GAMETITLE** (`KBHandlersCode.cpp`):
  In `SCENE_GAMETITLE`, pressing ESC while the `GamePlayTypes` or `DifficultyWindow` sub-window is open no longer exits the application. Instead it fades the active window out via `GUIManager::ApplyWindowFadeCallback()`, removes it, then recreates and fades in the `GameMenuWindow` — allowing the user to abort or correct a mistaken selection and return to the main menu. If neither sub-window is open the existing shutdown sequence (fade-to-black → quit) remains unchanged.
- *See: [`KBHandlersCode.cpp`](KBHandlersCode.cpp)*

- **Fix — `IncrementVersion.cmake` was resetting `CURRENT_BUILD_SUBVERSION` and `CURRENT_BUILD_VERSION` to 0 on every build** (`cmake/IncrementVersion.cmake`, `cmake-build.bat`, `Linux/cmake-build.sh`):
  Every cmake PRE_BUILD run of `IncrementVersion.cmake` reset major and subversion to hardcoded `0` regardless of what was in `Version.id`, because `set(MASTER_VER 0)` and `set(SUB_VER 0)` were static assignments and the regex only captured the third segment (`CMAKE_MATCH_1` = build number). Additionally, `cmake-build.bat`/`.sh` now also increments the version before calling cmake, so the CMake PRE_BUILD hook was firing a second time and double-incrementing the build number on top of the reset. Two fixes applied: (1) `IncrementVersion.cmake` now parses all three version segments from `Version.id` using `v([0-9]+)\\.([0-9]+)\\.([0-9]+)` and assigns `MASTER_VER = CMAKE_MATCH_1`, `SUB_VER = CMAKE_MATCH_2` — major and subversion are preserved exactly as stored in the file. (2) `cmake-build.bat` sets `SKIP_VERSION_INCREMENT=1` immediately before `cmake --build`; `cmake-build.sh` exports the same variable. `IncrementVersion.cmake` already checks `$ENV{SKIP_VERSION_INCREMENT}` and returns early when set, so the PRE_BUILD hook is now a no-op when invoked via the shell wrappers. When cmake is invoked directly (bypassing the wrappers), the hook still runs and correctly preserves all three version components.
- *See: [`cmake/IncrementVersion.cmake`](cmake/IncrementVersion.cmake), [`cmake-build.bat`](cmake-build.bat), [`Linux/cmake-build.sh`](Linux/cmake-build.sh)*

- **Feature — GUI Window Fade System: alpha-transparency fade-in / fade-out for all GUI windows across all 4 render pipelines** (`GUIManager.h`, `GUIManager.cpp`):
  Two new non-blocking methods added to `GUIManager`: `ApplyWindowFade(winfadeType, overTimePeriod, windowName)` (fire-and-forget) and `ApplyWindowFadeCallback(winfadeType, overTimePeriod, windowName, callback)` (fires a `std::function<void()>` lambda on completion). `GUIWindowFadeType` enum provides `FadeIn` (alpha 0→1, sets `isVisible=true` immediately) and `FadeOut` (alpha 1→0, sets `isVisible=false` on completion and resets `m_fadeAlpha` to 1.0 for the next show). Fade state is stored per `GUIWindow` as `WindowFadeState` (active flag, type, duration, `steady_clock::time_point` start, optional callback). Ticking is performed inside `GUIManager::Render()` under the mutex before the snapshot is built, so alpha is up-to-date for every rendered frame with zero extra thread overhead. Completed-fade callbacks are queued and fired **after** the mutex is released to prevent re-entrant deadlocks. The `GUIWindow::Render()` function applies fade via a local `fc()` lambda (`c.a = uint8_t(c.a * m_fadeAlpha)`) wrapping every `DrawRectangle`, `DrawTexture`, `DrawMyText`, and `DrawMyTextCentered` call — covering background, Button, TextArea, TitleBar, Scrollbar, ToggleSlider, and HSlider controls. Because alpha is applied at the colour-packing layer before the renderer API is called, the feature works identically across all four pipelines (DX11, DX12, OpenGL, Vulkan) with no renderer-specific code.
- *See: [`GUIManager.h`](GUIManager.h), [`GUIManager.cpp`](GUIManager.cpp)*

- **Fix — `cmake-build.bat` version increment now also updates `ReleaseInfo.md` header** (`cmake-build.bat`):
  The `*Current Build Version: vX.Y.Z*` line at the top of `ReleaseInfo.md` was not being updated when the build script incremented the version in `Version.id` and `BuildInfo.h`, causing the displayed version in the doc to drift behind after every build. Fixed by extending the existing version-increment PowerShell one-liner to also read `ReleaseInfo.md`, apply a regex replace on the `*Current Build Version:*` line, and write it back — all three files are now updated atomically within the same PowerShell invocation. The `SKIP_VERSION_INCREMENT` guard is unchanged, so `cmake-build all` still increments exactly once and all three files stay in sync.
- *See: [`cmake-build.bat`](cmake-build.bat)*

- **Feature — New GUI windows: `DifficultyWindow` and `GamePlayTypes`** (`GUIWindows.cpp`, `GUIManager.h`):
  Two new full-height right-side panel windows added, both matching the `GameMenuWindow` layout exactly (same `IMG_TITLEBAR2` title bar, `IMG_BUTTON2UP`/`IMG_BUTTON2DOWN` button textures, bold yellow shadowed text, hover effect). Buttons are centred both horizontally and vertically within the content area below the title bar using a dynamic runtime calculation based on `renderer->iOrigHeight`.
  **DifficultyWindow** — 5 active buttons: EASY, NORMAL, HARD, VERY HARD, MATE! (HELL). All handlers are TODO stubs ready for difficulty-state storage and onward navigation to `GamePlayTypes`. Call: `guiManager.CreateDifficultyWindow()`.
  **GamePlayTypes** — 7 buttons: CAMPAIGN (active, top-aligned at y+55 matching GameMenu), ARCADE, TIME RUSH, COCKPIT MODE, RANDOM, STAGE SELECT, and 1 LIFE MISSION (all 6 ghosted — grey semi-transparent text, hover texture locked to the up-state, `isClickHandled=false`, no mouse handlers). Ghosted buttons unlock after Campaign is fully completed. Campaign handler is a TODO stub. Call: `guiManager.CreateGamePlayTypesWindow()`.
- *See: [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp), [`GUIManager.h`](GUIManager.h)*

- **Fix — `GUIWindows.cpp`: C3493 compile errors — `GAMEPLAYTYPES_WINDOW_NAME` cannot be implicitly captured** (`GUIWindows.cpp`):
  All five difficulty-button `onMouseBtnDown` inner lambdas listed `GAMEPLAYTYPES_WINDOW_NAME` in their capture list as though it were a local variable. In C++ a constant (not a local variable or parameter) cannot be implicitly captured — MSVC raises `C3493`. Fixed by replacing the bare name in each capture list with an init-capture `gptName = std::string(GAMEPLAYTYPES_WINDOW_NAME)` (matching the pattern already used for `windowName` in the outer lambda) and updating the body to use `gptName`. All five occurrences replaced. Additionally fixed C2228 errors in the Easy and Normal button handlers: `player` is a `PlayerInfo*` but member accesses used `.` instead of `->` — all corrected to use `->` consistently with the Hard/VeryHard/Mate handlers. Additionally fixed a runtime SEH `0xC0000005` access violation when any difficulty button was clicked: all five handlers called `gamePlayer.GetPlayerInfo(PLAYER_1)` which returns `nullptr` because `InitPlayer()` has not been called before the difficulty screen is shown (no player slot is active yet) — dereferencing null caused the crash. Fixed by replacing `gamePlayer.GetPlayerInfo(PLAYER_1)` with `&playerInfo[PLAYER_1]` in all five handlers; `playerInfo[]` is a globally-initialised `PlayerInfo` array (`main.cpp` line 193) that is always valid and is the correct pre-game configuration target before a game session begins.
- *See: [`GUIWindows.cpp`](GUIWindows.cpp)*

- **Fix — GUI window fade now correctly fades textured buttons on DX11 and Vulkan** (`DX11Renderer.cpp`, `VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`):
  Textured buttons (and all blit controls) did not fade during `ApplyWindowFade` / `ApplyWindowFadeCallback` on DX11 and Vulkan, while the background rectangle and text labels faded correctly. Root cause: `GUIWindow::Render()` passes `tintColor.a` (a `uint8_t`, range 0–255) scaled by `m_fadeAlpha` to `DrawTexture()` as the D2D `DrawBitmap` opacity parameter, which expects a normalised `FLOAT` (0.0–1.0). On DX11, `tintColor.a` was passed directly without normalisation (`tintColor.a` = e.g. 127 → `DrawBitmap` received `127.0f`, clamped to 1.0 — always fully opaque). On Vulkan, `DrawTexture()` ignored `tintColor` entirely and delegated to `Blit2DObjectToSize()`, which hardcoded `1.0f` opacity. DX12 already normalised correctly (`tintColor.a / 255.0f`) and OpenGL's `Render2DQuad` also normalised in its `glUniform4f` call — those two pipelines were unaffected. Fixed by: (1) DX11 `DrawTexture()`: changing `tintColor.a` to `tintColor.a / 255.0f` in the `DrawBitmap` opacity argument; (2) Vulkan `DrawTexture()`: replacing the `Blit2DObjectToSize()` call with an inline D2D `DrawBitmap` that passes `tintColor.a / 255.0f` as opacity, consistent with the DX11 and DX12 patterns.
- *See: [`DX11Renderer.cpp`](DX11Renderer.cpp), [`VULKAN_Renderer.cpp`](VULKAN_Renderer.cpp)*

#### June 21, 2026

- **Feature — GLTFAnimator: `SetAnimationDirection`, `AtAnimationEndFrame`, `HoldAnimationAtFrame`** (`GLTFAnimator.h`, `GLTFAnimator.cpp`, `Models.h`):
  Three new animation-control functions added to `GLTFAnimator`. (1) `SetAnimationDirection(int parentModelID, AnimationDirection direction)` — sets the playback direction for an animation instance. `AnimationDirection` enum (added to `Models.h`) has four values: `NONE` (0, no-op), `FORWARD` (1, advance toward end), `REVERSE` (2, advance backward toward start), `BOUNCE` (3, forward to end then reverse to start). If `isLooping` is set for the parent ID, FORWARD and REVERSE wrap around seamlessly; BOUNCE repeats indefinitely. Without looping, FORWARD/REVERSE stop at their destination frame; BOUNCE completes one full forward+reverse cycle then stops. `UpdateAnimations` updated to apply direction-aware delta time: REVERSE negates the delta, BOUNCE flips the sign using a `bounceGoingForward` phase flag stored on `AnimationInstance`, and FORWARD/NONE use standard signed playback speed. `AnimationInstance` (Models.h) gains two new members: `direction` and `bounceGoingForward`. (2) `AtAnimationEndFrame(int parentModelID, int& frameIndex)` — returns `true` and sets `frameIndex` to the last keyframe index (from the first non-empty sampler) when `currentTime >= animationEndTime`; returns `false` otherwise. (3) `HoldAnimationAtFrame(int parentModelID, int frameIndex)` — pauses the animation (`isPlaying = false`) and seeks `currentTime` to the time of the given keyframe index (clamped to valid bounds), freezing the visual at that frame.
- *See: [`GLTFAnimator.h`](GLTFAnimator.h), [`GLTFAnimator.cpp`](GLTFAnimator.cpp), [`Models.h`](Models.h)*

#### June 23, 2026

- **Feature — SceneManager: `PutModelToScene()`** (`SceneManager.h`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  New public function `int PutModelToScene(std::wstring name, XMFLOAT3 atWorldCoords, bool bIncChildren, bool bStartAnim)` that retrieves a named model from the global `models[]` cache and injects it into the next available free slot(s) in `scene_models[]`. The model must pass all four readiness checks: `bGpuReady`, `m_isLoaded`, `bInitialized`, and `bIsDestroyed == false` (equivalent to `IsActive() && bGpuReady`). The search prefers scene-graph root entries (`iParentModelID == -1`) and falls back to the first name-match if no root is found. When `bIncChildren == true`, all primitive siblings stored in `models[]` whose `iParentModelID` equals the root's `cachedInstanceIndex` are also copied alongside the root, with their `iParentModelID` re-pointed to the new parent scene slot. The group is positioned at `atWorldCoords` by overriding the translation component of the world matrix (`_41`, `_42`, `_43`) while preserving existing rotation and scale. `SetupModelForRendering(sceneSlot)` and `ApplyDefaultLightingFromManager()` are called for each injected model, and each slot is marked `m_isLoaded = true`. The cache entry's `cachedInstanceIndex` is updated to the newly allocated slot. When `bStartAnim == true` and animations are loaded, `CreateAnimationInstance()` and `StartAnimation()` are called on the new parent scene ID using the model's `iAnimationIndex` (defaulting to 0 if unset). Returns the new parent `scene_models[]` ID on success, or `-1` on failure (model not found, not GPU-ready, or insufficient free slots).
- *See: [`SceneManager.h`](SceneManager.h), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Feature — SceneManager: `bCacheOnly` parameter on all scene parsers** (`SceneManager.h`, `SceneManager.cpp`):
  Added `bool bCacheOnly = false` to `ParseSceneAutoDetect()`, `ParseGLBScene()`, `ParseGLTFScene()`, and `ParseFBXScene()`. When `true`, models are fully initialised and GPU-uploaded into the global `models[]` precache pool exactly as a normal load, but `scene_models[]` is left empty so nothing renders — the scene is treated as a dynamic scene built at runtime via `PutModelToScene()`. Cache-restore fast-paths also short-circuit their `scene_models[]` restore loop when `bCacheOnly` is set, returning immediately once session state (cameras, lights, animations) has been refreshed.
- *See: [`SceneManager.h`](SceneManager.h), [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Feature — FBXAnimator: native FBX animation playback** (`FBXAnimator.h`, `FBXAnimator.cpp`):
  New class `FBXAnimator` provides production-quality FBX animation playback directly from native FBX data structures, replacing the previous non-functional stub that tried to inject GLTF-converted clips into `GLTFAnimator` (which had no injection API). Parses all `FBXAnimStack` → `FBXAnimLayer` → `FBXAnimCurveNode` → `FBXAnimCurve` hierarchies into `FBXAnimationClip` / `FBXAnimChannel` structures at scene-load time. Per-frame evaluation: `EvaluateCurve()` converts seconds to FBX time units and performs step/linear interpolation using `keyAttrFlags` (bit 0x02 = constant, otherwise linear). Translation channels apply `ApplyCoordFlip()` (Z-negate for right-handed → left-handed Y-up). Rotation channels add `preRotation` in degrees, convert via `EulerToMatrix()` supporting all 6 rotation orders, apply `ApplyRotationFlip()` (M·R·M similarity transform with M = diag(1,1,-1)), then extract a DirectX row-vector quaternion via `MatrixToQuaternion()`. Public interface mirrors `GLTFAnimator` exactly: `StartAnimation`, `StopAnimation`, `PauseAnimation`, `ResumeAnimation`, `UpdateAnimations`, `ForceAnimationReset`, `SetAnimationSpeed`, `SetAnimationLooping`, `SetAnimationTime`, `SetAnimationDirection`, `AtAnimationEndFrame`, `HoldAnimationAtFrame`, `GetAnimationCount`, `GetClip`, `IsAnimationPlaying`, `GetAnimationTime`, `ClearAllAnimations`. Hierarchy helpers `ResetLocalTRSToBase`, `RecomposeWorldFromLocalTRS`, and `IsInHierarchy` match the `GLTFAnimator` pattern. Non-DirectX builds receive a complete `XMFLOAT4X4`, `XMMatrixRotationX/Y/Z`, `XMConvertToRadians`, `XMQuaternionRotationMatrix` stub block.
- *See: [`FBXAnimator.h`](FBXAnimator.h), [`FBXAnimator.cpp`](FBXAnimator.cpp)*

- **Feature — ModelAnimator: universal animation dispatcher** (`ModelAnimator.h`, `ModelAnimator.cpp`):
  New class `ModelAnimator` owns one `GLTFAnimator gltfAnimator` and one `FBXAnimator fbxAnimator` as public members and exposes a single unified interface that automatically routes each call to the correct sub-animator based on `ModelInfo::importType`. `SetModels(scene_models, MAX_SCENE_MODELS)` binds the scene array once from `SceneManager::Initialize()`; `UpdateAnimations(float deltaTime)` then advances both sub-animators without requiring callers to pass the model array. `IsAnimationPlaying(id)` returns true when either sub-animator has an active instance. `StartAnimation(id, clip)` dispatches by `importType`: `GLTF` → `gltfAnimator`, `FBX` → `fbxAnimator`, unknown → tries whichever has clips loaded. `Stop`, `Pause`, `Resume`, `SetAnimationSpeed/Looping/Time/Direction`, `HoldAnimationAtFrame`, and `ForceAnimationReset` call both sub-animators safely (the one without an instance is a no-op). `ClearAllAnimations()` clears both. `SceneManager::gltfAnimator` has been replaced with `SceneManager::modelAnimator`; all 30+ internal call sites updated.
- *See: [`ModelAnimator.h`](ModelAnimator.h), [`ModelAnimator.cpp`](ModelAnimator.cpp)*

- **Feature — Models.h: `ImportType` enum + FBX-specific `ModelInfo` fields**:
  Added `enum class ImportType : int { NONE=0, GLTF=1, FBX=2 }` after `AnimationDirection`. Added three fields to `ModelInfo`: `ImportType importType = ImportType::NONE` (set automatically at parse time for dispatch), `int fbxNodeIndex = -1` (index into `FBXScene::models[]`), and `std::string fbxNodeName` (FBX model name for post-load rebinding and debug). `importType` is set to `ImportType::GLTF` at every `gltfNodeIndex` assignment in `ParseGLBNodeRecursive` and `ParseGLTFNodeRecursive`, and to `ImportType::FBX` at every `fbxIDToSlot` assignment in `ParseFBXScene`.
- *See: [`Models.h`](Models.h)*

- **Fix — SceneManager: FBX animation now plays** (`SceneManager.cpp`):
  `ParseFBXScene()` animation section (previously a non-functional stub) replaced with a call to `modelAnimator.fbxAnimator.ParseAnimationsFromFBX(fbx, fbxIDToSlot)` followed by auto-start of each parsed clip on the root model. Root resolution walks the parent chain from `clip->channels[0].targetModelSlot` upward. `UpdateSceneAnimations()` now calls `modelAnimator.UpdateAnimations(deltaTime)` (the unified dispatcher) instead of the GLTF-only path.
- *See: [`SceneManager.cpp`](SceneManager.cpp)*

- **Update — All renderer frame files: unified animation dispatch** (`DXRenderFrame.cpp`, `DX12RenderFrame.cpp`, `VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`, `OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`):
  Replaced `scene.gltfAnimator.IsAnimationPlaying(id)` → `scene.modelAnimator.IsAnimationPlaying(id)` and `scene.gltfAnimator.UpdateAnimations(deltaTime, scene.scene_models, MAX_MODELS)` → `scene.modelAnimator.UpdateAnimations(deltaTime)` in all four render frame files. The new calls handle GLTF and FBX animated models automatically with no format-specific branching required in render code.
- *See: [`DXRenderFrame.cpp`](DXRenderFrame.cpp), [`DX12RenderFrame.cpp`](DX12RenderFrame.cpp), [`VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp`](VULKAN_RenderFrame.cpp), [`OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp`](OpenGLRenderFrame.cpp)*

- **Visual — ConsoleWindow: full 3D panel rendering** (`ConsoleWindow.cpp`):
  Replaced the flat `DrawRectangle` chrome with GUIManager-matching 3D bevel rendering throughout. Window container gains a drop shadow (+4px offset, 90 alpha) and a double-bevel raised border (outer: highlight `(88,94,118)` / shadow `(8,10,18)`, inner: `(60,65,84)` / `(14,16,26)`). Title bar is now a solid 3D raised panel — no images — with a base blue fill, a semi-transparent upper-half lighter overlay for a vertical gradient effect, a 2px top sheen strip, and the same double outer+inner raised bevel. Scrollbar track uses the matching sunken bevel style (`DrawSunkenPanel`). Scrollbar thumb is a raised mini-panel with drop shadow and four-edge highlight/shadow lines. The command-bar separator is now a two-pixel ridge line (dark groove + light counter-edge). The command bar uses `DrawRaisedPanel` for consistency with dialog panels. Both helper lambdas (`DrawRaisedPanel`, `DrawSunkenPanel`) are defined inline in `RenderContent` using identical colour constants to the GUIManager Panel control renderer.
- *See: [`ConsoleWindow.cpp`](ConsoleWindow.cpp)*

- **Visual — ConsoleWindow: wider scrollbar, richer title shading, semi-transparent body** (`ConsoleWindow.h`, `ConsoleWindow.cpp`):
  `CONSOLE_SCROLLBAR_W` increased from 10 to 16 px for easier grabbing. Title bar replaced with a four-zone gradient: dark base → lower-third darkening band → upper-half lighter band → 2px top sheen strip (`alpha 110`), creating a strong light-top/dark-bottom 3D depth effect without images. Content body alpha reduced from 218 to 178 (~70%) so the scene behind the console shows through.
- *See: [`ConsoleWindow.h`](ConsoleWindow.h), [`ConsoleWindow.cpp`](ConsoleWindow.cpp)*

- **Feature — ConsoleWindow: `close` and `top` built-in commands** (`ConsoleWindow.cpp`):
  `close` hides the console by calling `Toggle()`. `top` scrolls the buffer to the oldest entry by setting `m_scrollOffset` to the maximum possible offset (`totalLines - visibleLines`).
- *See: [`ConsoleWindow.cpp`](ConsoleWindow.cpp)*

- **Feature — GUIManager: Panel, TextInput, ListBox, ComboBox control types** (`GUIManager.h`, `GUIManager.cpp`):
  Four new `GUIControlType` values added — all rendered purely via `DrawRectangle` / `DrawMyText` with multi-layer bevel edges and drop shadows for maximum 3D depth on all four pipelines. **Panel**: raised (sliderValue >= 0.5) or sunken (< 0.5) decorative background with 2-level bevel and optional drop shadow; purely non-interactive. **TextInput**: single-line editable field with sunken frame, focus glow ring, blinking cursor bar (cursor position calculated from per-character width via `GetCharacterWidth`), placeholder text support; receives input via `onCharInput` / `onBackspace`; clicking auto-focuses and positions cursor at click point. **ListBox**: scrollable item list with embedded 12px scrollbar (3D raised thumb with grip lines, alternating row shading, blue selection highlight, gold tint for entries beginning with `►`); scrollbar thumb can be click-dragged; mouse-wheel auto-routing added to `GUIManager::HandleMouseWheel` when no `onMouseWheel` override is registered. **ComboBox**: closed state shows selected text and ▼ button; open dropdown rendered in a mandatory **second pass** after the main control loop so it paints on top of all controls; clicking outside the dropdown in the pre-pass automatically closes it.
- *See: [`GUIManager.h`](GUIManager.h), [`GUIManager.cpp`](GUIManager.cpp)*

- **Feature — GUIFileDialog: Windows 11-style Load and Save dialogs** (`GUIFileDialog.cpp` — new file):
  `GUIManager::CreateLoadDialog()` and `GUIManager::CreateSaveDialog()` open a centered, modal, 720×480 file dialog matching the Windows 11 Open/Save dialog layout using only CPGE GUI controls. The dialog consists of: a draggable 3D title bar with [X] close; a navigation bar with Back (◄), Forward (►), Up (▲) buttons (full history stack) and a read-only address label; a Quick Access left sidebar (Desktop, Documents, Downloads, Pictures, Music, This PC via `SHGetFolderPathW`); column headers (Name, Date Modified, Type, Size); a 3D `ListBox` file list (directories coloured gold and navigate on click; files populate the filename field); a `TextInput` filename field with full keyboard entry; a `ComboBox` file-type filter that re-scans on change; primary Open/Save button (blue) and Cancel button. Enter key confirms or navigates into a directory (load mode). Filter patterns support `*.*`, `*.ext` style matching. Only one Load and one Save dialog can be open at a time; a second call brings the existing dialog to front. All background chrome uses `Panel` controls ordered first in the control list so they render behind interactive controls.
- *See: [`GUIFileDialog.cpp`](GUIFileDialog.cpp), [`GUIManager.h`](GUIManager.h), [`Docs/GUIManager-Example-Usage.md`](Docs/GUIManager-Example-Usage.md)*

- **Docs — SceneManager-Example-Usage.md: ModelAnimator and FBXAnimator documentation**:
  Updated title, core-concepts section, FBX animation limitation note (removed — FBX now fully supported), and the entire Animations section. New content covers the `ModelAnimator` dispatcher architecture diagram, `ImportType` auto-dispatch explanation, updated code examples using `scene.modelAnimator.*`, FBX vs GLTF feature comparison, and guidance for accessing the sub-animators directly for format-specific APIs.
- *See: [`Docs/SceneManager-Example-Usage.md`](Docs/SceneManager-Example-Usage.md)*

- **Fix — FBXAnimator: OpenGL build compile errors** (`FBXAnimator.cpp`):
  Three C2062/C2143/C2447 errors on OpenGL builds caused by a redundant `inline float XMConvertToRadians(float deg)` stub on line 30. `Includes.h` defines `XMConvertToRadians` as a function-like macro outside the `CPGE_MATH_STUBS_DEFINED` guard, so it is always active for all targets. When the preprocessor then encountered the inline function declaration with the same name, it expanded the macro into the declaration text, producing unparseable output. Fix: removed the inline function; the `Includes.h` macro provides identical behaviour.
- *See: [`FBXAnimator.cpp`](FBXAnimator.cpp)*

- **Fix — FXManager: firework rocket centre-drift now gradual across all pipelines** (`DX_FXManager.cpp`, `DX12FXManager.cpp`, `OpenGLFXManager.cpp`, `VULKAN_FXManager.cpp`):
  The horizontal centre-pull previously triggered abruptly at 75% of the ascent and ramped to full force in the final 25%, causing a visually jarring snap. Changed to start at 30% of travel with `curvePhase = (travelProgress - 0.30f) / 0.70f` so the drift ramps over 70% of the flight; pull force reduced from `0.002f` to `0.0003f`; damping eased from `0.90f` to `0.95f`, producing a smooth, barely-perceptible arc rather than an abrupt turn.
- *See: [`DX_FXManager.cpp`](DX_FXManager.cpp), [`DX12FXManager.cpp`](DX12FXManager.cpp), [`OpenGLFXManager.cpp`](OpenGLFXManager.cpp), [`VULKAN_FXManager.cpp`](VULKAN_FXManager.cpp)*

- **Enhancement — FXManager: 3D sphere firework explosions with particle trails** (`DX_FXManager.h`, `DX12FXManager.h`, `OpenGLFXManager.h`, `VULKAN_FXManager.h`, `DX_FXManager.cpp`, `DX12FXManager.cpp`, `OpenGLFXManager.cpp`, `VULKAN_FXManager.cpp`):
  Overhauled firework particle dispersion and rendering across all four render pipelines. `FireworkParticle` gains two new fields — `screenDX` and `screenDY` — storing the precomputed 2D screen-space direction vector from a Fibonacci sphere distribution, replacing the previous per-particle random angle. Each explosion now spawns exactly 72 particles (previously 10–45 random) placed with a golden-angle Fibonacci lattice so particles fan out uniformly over a 3D sphere projected onto the screen, giving a consistent spherical burst shape every time. The `FastSinCos` per-frame position calculation is removed; particle position is now `explodeX + screenDX * radius`, `explodeY + screenDY * radius` — no trig per frame. Explosion radius retains per-rocket randomness (50–120 px) and colour remains fully random per burst. `DrawFireworksPixels` updated for all renderers: rockets now draw a 5-step fading ascent trail below the head; exploded particles draw 6 inward trail segments (5 px apart) along the exact radial path with quadratic alpha fade and decreasing pixel size, producing a glowing streak behind each star identical to real fireworks.
- *See: [`DX_FXManager.h`](DX_FXManager.h), [`DX12FXManager.h`](DX12FXManager.h), [`OpenGLFXManager.h`](OpenGLFXManager.h), [`VULKAN_FXManager.h`](VULKAN_FXManager.h), [`DX_FXManager.cpp`](DX_FXManager.cpp), [`DX12FXManager.cpp`](DX12FXManager.cpp), [`OpenGLFXManager.cpp`](OpenGLFXManager.cpp), [`VULKAN_FXManager.cpp`](VULKAN_FXManager.cpp)*

- **Feature — ThreadManager: Windows multi-core scheduling system** (`ThreadManager.h`, `ThreadManager.cpp`, `main.cpp`):
  Introduced a complete Windows multi-core thread scheduling infrastructure to the engine's threading layer. **`ThreadSchedulingConfig`** (Windows-only): new struct holding `DWORD idealCore`, `int priority`, and `bool useEngineDefaults`. When `useEngineDefaults=true` (the default), `SetThread()` automatically applies the recommended LP assignment and priority for each known `ThreadNameID` — no changes required in existing renderer, FileIO, AI, or network callers. **`ThreadUtils`** (Windows-only static class): `NameCurrentThread(wchar_t*)` registers the OS-level thread description visible in VS 2022, PIX, RenderDoc, and WPA via `SetThreadDescription()`; `PreferCore(DWORD)` applies a soft ideal-processor hint via `SetThreadIdealProcessor()` with bounds validation; `ForceCore(DWORD)` applies hard affinity via `SetThreadAffinityMask()` (debug/profiling only); `SetPriority(int)` calls `SetThreadPriority()`; `GetLogicalProcessorCount()` queries `GetSystemInfo()`. **`SetThread()` updated**: extended signature accepts optional `const ThreadSchedulingConfig& scheduling = {}`. Inside the thread lambda, `NameCurrentThread()`, `PreferCore()`, and `SetPriority()` are applied automatically based on engine defaults: AI → LP 1 NORMAL, Renderer → LP 2 ABOVE_NORMAL, Loader → LP 3 NORMAL, FileIO → LP 4 NORMAL, Network → LP 5 NORMAL. Scheduling calls are made from inside the new thread (not the creator) so `GetCurrentThread()` resolves correctly.
